        <meta property="og:url" content="https://pubs.acs.org/doi/full/10.1021/acsami.1c16316"><meta property="og:title" content="Minimal TiO2 Coupled with Conductive Polymer-Stimulated Synergistic Effect on Fast and Reversible Sodium-Ion Storage for Bismuth Sulfide"><meta property="og:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c16316/asset/images/acsami.1c16316.social.jpeg_v03"><meta property="og:description" content="Designing multiphase composition is believed to availably boost the structural integrity and electrochemical properties of sodium-ion battery anodes. Herein, a conceive of nanoflowers, assembled with Bi2S3 nanorods, is demonstrated to construct the multiphase composition involving TiO2 coating and polypyrrole (PPy) encapsulation. Bi2S3 acted as the dominating active material, in consideration of the low content of TiO2, which ensured the high capacity of the composite. The dual-structural restrain of the TiO2 and PPy coatings can effectively alleviate volume variation based on the pseudo-“zero-strain” effect of TiO2 and high flexibility of PPy shells. Meanwhile, the heterointerface greatly enhanced the coupling effect between Bi2S3 and TiO2 and thus improved the electrochemical performance, which was proved by the results of density functional theory calculation and electrochemical tests. Combining the regulation from the Bi2S3/TiO2 heterojunction and the dual-structural restrain effect, the Bi2S3/TiO2@PPy electrode exhibited excellent rate performance and superior cycle stability (275.8 mA h g–1 over 500 cycles at 10 A g–1). This study indicates that designing multiphase composition can be very promising and provides a structural insight to construct high stability in electrodes for sodium-ion batteries."><meta property="og:type" content="Article"><meta property="og:site_name" content="ACS Publications"><meta name="twitter:card" content="summary_large_image"><meta name="twitter:site" content="@ACSPublications"><meta name="twitter:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c16316/asset/images/acsami.1c16316.social.jpeg_v03">

<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/wro/nwyw~thiss-ds.js" async="" nonce="90da8870ed46b325-SJC"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="90da8870ed46b325-SJC">

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            timeout: 5000,

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
            },
            retrieveEntity: function (ms) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                if (ms == undefined || ms === '') {
                    ms = this.timeout;
                }

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res.data);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('failed to retrieve entity from local storage: ' + err);
                        });
                    // Set up the timeout
                    setTimeout(function () {
                        reject('Promise timed out ' + ms + ' ms');
                    }, ms);
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage due to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {
                            doi: doi,
                            entityid: entityId,
                            entityTitle: entityTitle,
                            eventGroupKey: '914c41c8-a0a6-40b6-ade4-5426a0450305'
                        }

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    }).fail(function (status) {
                        return reject(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (i = 0; i < allSsoInstitutions.length; i++) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        if(allSsoInstitutions.length === 0 && true){
                            self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, null, null)
                                .then(function () {
                                    console.log('No Entity found');
                                }, function (err) {
                                    console.log('failed to get the none entity status' ,err);
                                });
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            }).catch(function (err) {
                                reject(err);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();

                    if ($('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').length > 0) {
                        let institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox = $('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').get(0);
                        if (!$(institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox).is(":checked")) {
                            return;
                        }
                    }

                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

        <script async="" type="text/javascript" src="https://www.googletagservices.com/tag/js/gpt.js" rel="preconnect" nonce="90da8870ed46b325-SJC"></script>

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="90da8870ed46b325-SJC">
var dfpReady = false;
$(document).ready(function() {
    // var journalTitle = 'applied_materials_interfaces';
    var taxonomyKeywords = $('.article_header-taxonomy');
    var articleKeyword = $('meta[name="keywords"]');
    var articleTitle = $('meta[name="dc.Title"]');
    var articleDescription = $('meta[name="dc.Description"]');
    var abstractKeyword = $('p.articleBody_abstractText:contains("Keywords: ")');
    var searchTerms = [];

    if (taxonomyKeywords.length > 0) {
        $(taxonomyKeywords).children(".rlist--inline").children("li").each(function() {
            searchTerms.push($(this).text());
        });
    }
    else if (articleKeyword.length > 0) { 
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleKeyword.prop('content').split(', '));
    }
    else if (abstractKeyword.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(abstractKeyword.text().split("Keywords: ")[1].split('; '));
    }
    else if (articleDescription.length > 0) {
        $(articleDescription).each(function() {
            articleDescriptionKeywords = $(this).prop('content');
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/.,/g,"");
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/\s{2,}/g," ");
            searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleDescriptionKeywords.split(' '));
        });
    }

    if (articleTitle.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleTitle.prop('content').split(' '));
    }

    googletag.cmd.push(function() {
        var mappingLeader = googletag.sizeMapping().
        addSize([750, 200], [728, 90]). 
        addSize([0, 0], [320, 50]).
        build();
        //leaderboard
        googletag.defineSlot('/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article', [728, 90], 'dfp-journal-article-leaderboard').defineSizeMapping(mappingLeader).setTargeting('location', 'leaderboard1').setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //recommend
        googletag.defineSlot("/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article", [1, 1], "dfp-journal-article-recommend").setTargeting("ntvPlacement", ["1100167"]).setTargeting("location", "recommend").setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //googletag.pubads().enableSingleRequest();
        googletag.pubads().collapseEmptyDivs();
        googletag.pubads().setTargeting('inst',dartInstitutionType).setTargeting('memb',dartMember);
        googletag.pubads().addEventListener("slotRenderEnded", function(event) {
            console.log(event.slot.getSlotElementId() + " isEmpty: " + event.isEmpty + " | creative id: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            if((event.isEmpty === false) && (event.slot.getSlotElementId() != "dfp-journal-article-recommend")) {
                $("#" + event.slot.getSlotElementId()).parents(".advertisement").slideDown();
                console.log("ad display: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            }
            // else {
            //     console.log("no ad found");
            // }
        });
        googletag.enableServices();
        dfpReady = true;
    });
});
</script>

href="/action/showCitFormats?doi=10.1021/acsami.1c16316&amp;href=/doi/10.1021/acsami.1c16316" title="Cite This" class="figure-viewer-cite-this-link"><i class="icon-check-circle"></i><span><strong>Cite <script nonce="90da8870ed46b325-SJC">
$(function() {
    var serialCode = "aamick";
    var books = ["reagents", "symposium", "advances", "medichemreviews", "styleguide"]
    if(books.includes(serialCode) === false) {
        // default click action
        $("[data-id]").on("mousedown", function(e) {
            var currentClickID = $(this).attr("data-id");

            if(currentClickID.includes("_hover") === false) {
                if(currentClickID.match("^article_") && !currentClickID.match("^article_abstract_CC")) {   
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Minimal TiO&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Coupled with Conductive Polymer-Stimulated Synergistic Effect on Fast and Reversible Sodium-Ion Storage for Bismuth Sulfide", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.1c16316", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                }
            }
        });
        
        // Access Management icons hover
        var articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        var articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent === false) {
                articleAccessManagementIconHover = true;
                var articleAccessManagementHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleAccessManagementIconHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Minimal TiO&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Coupled with Conductive Polymer-Stimulated Synergistic Effect on Fast and Reversible Sodium-Ion Storage for Bismuth Sulfide", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.1c16316", "Article_Element": articleAccessManagementHover });
    
                        articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        });
    
        // articleRightsPermissionsLink hover
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent === false) {
                articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = true;
                var articleRightsHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Minimal TiO&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Coupled with Conductive Polymer-Stimulated Synergistic Effect on Fast and Reversible Sodium-Ion Storage for Bismuth Sulfide", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.1c16316", "Article_Element": articleRightsHover });
    
                        articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        });
    
        // Author hover
        var articleAuthorHover = false
        var articleAuthorHoverEvent = false
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if((articleAuthorHoverEvent === false) && ($(this).parent().hasClass("view-affs") === false)) {
                articleAuthorHover = true;
                var authorInfoHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAuthorHover === true) && (articleAuthorHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Minimal TiO&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Coupled with Conductive Polymer-Stimulated Synergistic Effect on Fast and Reversible Sodium-Ion Storage for Bismuth Sulfide", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.1c16316", "Article_Element": authorInfoHover });
    
                        articleAuthorHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAuthorHover = false;
        });
    
        // CC License hover
        var articleAbstractCCHover = false
        var articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = false
        var articleDrawerCCHover = false
        var articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = false
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if($(this).attr("data-id")) {
                if(($(this).attr("data-id") === "article_drawer_CC-License") && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleDrawerCCHover = true;
                    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleDrawerCCHover === true) && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Minimal TiO&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Coupled with Conductive Polymer-Stimulated Synergistic Effect on Fast and Reversible Sodium-Ion Storage for Bismuth Sulfide", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.1c16316", "Article_Element": "article_drawer_CC-License_hover" });
    
                            articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
                else if(($(this).attr("data-id").match("^article_abstract_CC")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleAbstractCCHover = true;
    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Minimal TiO&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Coupled with Conductive Polymer-Stimulated Synergistic Effect on Fast and Reversible Sodium-Ion Storage for Bismuth Sulfide", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.1c16316", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                            articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
            }
            else if(($(this).hasClass("article__cc-license__link")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = true;
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Minimal TiO&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Coupled with Conductive Polymer-Stimulated Synergistic Effect on Fast and Reversible Sodium-Ion Storage for Bismuth Sulfide", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.1c16316", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                        articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            if(articleAbstractCCHover === true) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = false;
            }
            if(articleDrawerCCHover = true) {
                articleDrawerCCHover = false;
            }
        });
        
        // show recommeneded click delay
        var intervalCount = 0;
        var showRecommendedInterval = setInterval(function() {
            intervalCount += 100;
            if($(".show-recommended__wrapper .show-recommended").length > 0) {
                clearInterval(showRecommendedInterval);
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowMore']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Minimal TiO&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Coupled with Conductive Polymer-Stimulated Synergistic Effect on Fast and Reversible Sodium-Ion Storage for Bismuth Sulfide", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.1c16316", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowLess']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Minimal TiO&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Coupled with Conductive Polymer-Stimulated Synergistic Effect on Fast and Reversible Sodium-Ion Storage for Bismuth Sulfide", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.1c16316", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
            }
        }, 100);
    }
});
</script>

href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D55051%26pageCount%3D9%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DHui%2BGuan%252C%2BXin%2BDu%252C%2BYuhao%2BYi%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D13%26issueNum%3D46%26contentID%3Dacsami.1c16316%26title%3DMinimal%2BTiO2%2BCoupled%2Bwith%2BConductive%2BPolymer-Stimulated%2BSynergistic%2BEffect%2Bon%2BFast%2Band%2BReversible%2BSodium-Ion%2BStorage%2Bfor%2BBismuth%2BSulfide%26numPages%3D9%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1944-8244%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Daamick%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D55059%26publicationDate%3DNovember%2B2021" Empty dropzone --></div></div></div></div><div class="article_abstract"><div class="article_abstract-title" id="Abstract" tabindex="0"><h2>Abstract</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div><div class="article_abstract-content hlFld-Abstract" id="abstractBox" property="description"><figure id="_i1" data-index="0" class="article__inlineFigure article_abstract-img"><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img class="inline-fig internalNav" src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c16316/asset/images/medium/am1c16316_0008.gif" alt="" id="tgr1" property="image" style="width:405px; height:275px"></button><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c16316/asset/images/large/am1c16316_0008.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.1c16316&amp;id=_i1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p class="articleBody_abstractText">Designing multiphase composition is believed to availably boost the structural integrity and electrochemical properties of sodium-ion battery anodes. Herein, a conceive of nanoflowers, assembled with Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> nanorods, is demonstrated to construct the multiphase composition involving TiO<sub>2</sub> coating and polypyrrole (PPy) encapsulation. Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> acted as the dominating active material, in consideration of the low content of TiO<sub>2</sub>, which ensured the high capacity of the composite. The dual-structural restrain of the TiO<sub>2</sub> and PPy coatings can effectively alleviate volume variation based on the pseudo-“zero-strain” effect of TiO<sub>2</sub> and high flexibility of PPy shells. Meanwhile, the heterointerface greatly enhanced the coupling effect between Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> and TiO<sub>2</sub> and thus improved the electrochemical performance, which was proved by the results of density functional theory calculation and electrochemical tests. Combining the regulation from the Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub> heterojunction and the dual-structural restrain effect, the Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy electrode exhibited excellent rate performance and superior cycle stability (275.8 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> over 500 cycles at 10 A g<sup>–1</sup>). This study indicates that designing multiphase composition can be very promising and provides a structural insight to construct high stability in electrodes for sodium-ion batteries.</p></div><div class="article__cc-license"><div class="article__cc-license__body"><p class="article__cc-license__para">This publication is licensed under the terms of your
                            institutional subscription.
                            <a href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D55051%26pageCount%3D9%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DHui%2BGuan%252C%2BXin%2BDu%252C%2BYuhao%2BYi%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D13%26issueNum%3D46%26contentID%3Dacsami.1c16316%26title%3DMinimal%2BTiO2%2BCoupled%2Bwith%2BConductive%2BPolymer-Stimulated%2BSynergistic%2BEffect%2Bon%2BFast%2Band%2BReversible%2BSodium-Ion%2BStorage%2Bfor%2BBismuth%2BSulfide%26numPages%3D9%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1944-8244%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Daamick%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D55059%26publicationDate%3DNovember%2B2021" class="link--bold">Request reuse permissions.</a></p></div></div><span class="hidden" property="publisher">ACS Publications</span><div class="article_header-article-copyright">Copyright © 2021 American Chemical Society</div><div class="article_header-footer-right"><div class="articleHeaderDropzone7" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone7"><div class="article__tags article__tags--subjects"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Subjects</h3><div tabindex="0" class="article__tags__tooltip"><div aria-describedby="tooltip-subjects" class="article__tags__icon"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are subjects</span></div><p id="tooltip-subjects" role="tooltip" class="article__tags__diff">Article subjects are automatically applied from the ACS Subject Taxonomy and describe the scientific concepts and themes of the article.</p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291557&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Coating materials" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Coating%20materials" class="article__tags__link">Coating materials</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291331&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Composites" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Composites" class="article__tags__link">Composites</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291371&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Electrodes" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Electrodes" class="article__tags__link">Electrodes</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291503&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Organic polymers" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Organic%20polymers" class="article__tags__link">Organic polymers</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=290689&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Oxides" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Oxides" class="article__tags__link">Oxides</a></li></ul></div></div></div></div><div class="article__tags article__tags--keywords hlFld-Abstract"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Keywords</h3><div class="article__tags__tooltip" tabindex="0"><div class="article__tags__icon" aria-describedby="tooltip-keywords"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are keywords</span></div><p class="article__tags__diff" id="tooltip-keywords" role="tooltip">
                        Article keywords are supplied by the authors and highlight key terms and topics
                        of the paper.
                    </p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Sodium-ion+Batteries&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_sodium-ion%20batteries">sodium-ion batteries</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Anode+Material&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_anode%20material">anode material</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Bi2s3&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_Bi2S3">Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub></a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Bi2s3%2Ftio2%40ppy&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_Bi2S3%2FTiO2%40PPy">Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Heterojunction+Interface&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_heterojunction%20interface">heterojunction interface</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="article_content"><div class="article_content-table hlFld-FullText"><div class="article_content-row"><div class="article_content-left" property="articleBody" style="width: 384px;"><div id="sec1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i2">Introduction</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">The worldwide issues of climate and energy crisis have aroused tremendous concerns and enthusiasm in the electrochemical energy storage systems, for instance, cellular phones, computers, and other electrical devices. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref1 ref2 ref3 ref4 ref5'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref1 ref2 ref3 ref4 ref5" aria-label="reference 1 to 5">(1−5)</a> Lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) have been taking an in-depth study recently on account of high energy density as one of the most widely used battery systems. Nonetheless, the application of LIBs is strongly influenced by limited lithium sources in the long run. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref6 ref7 ref8 ref9 ref10'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref6 ref7 ref8 ref9 ref10" aria-label="reference 6 to 10">(6−10)</a> Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are gaining traction by reason of the abundant resources and their similar intercalation chemistry to LIBs. However, the larger sodium ionic radius compared with that of lithium usually results in the depressed reaction dynamics and huge volumetric expansion/extraction of the electrode material. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref11 ref12 ref13 ref14'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref11 ref12 ref13 ref14" aria-label="reference 11 to 14">(11−14)</a> Thus, there are lots of researchers focusing on the study of advanced SIB anodes.</div><div class="NLM_p">Recently, metal oxides and metal sulfides have attracted extensive attention by reason of high theoretical capacities, rich sources, and low price. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15 ref16 ref17 ref18 ref19 ref20'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref15 ref16 ref17 ref18 ref19 ref20" aria-label="reference 15 to 20">(15−20)</a> Therefore, the VA metal-based elements have been in the spotlight and have achieved some positive results. The examples include 3D Ni-supported Sb<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref21" aria-label="reference 21">(21)</a> multishell structured Sb<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref22" aria-label="reference 22">(22)</a> 2D layered As<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref23" aria-label="reference 23">(23)</a> Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>@SC hollow nanotubes, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref24" aria-label="reference 24">(24)</a> topological insulator Bi<sub>2</sub>Te<sub>3</sub>, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref25" aria-label="reference 25">(25)</a> and so on. Thereinto, Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>, as a popular semiconductor material, tends to grow in one-dimensional (1D) direction and therefore form the 1D nanostructures, such as nanotubes, nanobelts, and nanofibers, and thus the directional migration of ions. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref26 ref27 ref28'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref26 ref27 ref28" aria-label="reference 26 to 28">(26−28)</a> Theoretically, Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> can provide a capacity of 625 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> (4250 mA h cm<sup>–3</sup>) as an anode. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref29" aria-label="reference 29">(29)</a> However, its severe volume expansion/extraction during the charge/discharge process and intrinsically low electrical conductivity result in the pulverization of the electrode material, sluggish ion transfer, and consequently poor electrochemical performance. In the past decade, many strategies have been explored to overcome these shortcomings. For instance, Cao et al. fabricated the Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/MoS<sub>2</sub> bimetallic sulfide compound with abundant phase boundaries, which successfully kept the material integrity and displayed long cycle life. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref30" aria-label="reference 30">(30)</a> Huang et al. designed and synthesized MOF-derived Co<sub>9</sub>S<sub>8</sub>-coated Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> spheres with the N-carbon external layer, showing enhanced electrical conductivity and depressed volumetric variation. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref31" aria-label="reference 31">(31)</a> As noted above, the regulation of multiphase compounds, in which different phases play the role as the buffer and conductive network, has a positive impact on relieving the volume variation in the process of ion insertion/extraction.</div><div class="NLM_p last">Herein, we report a Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy composite as-prepared via a two-step coating process by a facile wet chemistry method at room temperature. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref32" aria-label="reference 32">(32)</a> The TiO<sub>2</sub> covered on Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> nanorods can function as a supporting sheath to maintain structural stability owing to its good physicochemical stability. Moreover, it can form heterojunction with Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> to introduce the build-in electric field to enhance electrical conductivity and improve reaction kinetics. To further enhance the electrical conductivity and alleviate the volumetric change of the Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub> composite, we chose the conductive polymer of polypyrrole (PPy) as the external coating layer on account of its high conductivity, low price, and synthesis facility. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref33" aria-label="reference 33">(33)</a> As a result, the Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy composite is expected to show a superior electrochemical capability.</div></div><div id="sec2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i3">2.  Experimental Section</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div id="sec2_1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i4" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i4">2.1.  Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> Nanorod Fabrication</h3><div class="NLM_p last">Typically, 0.4 g of polyvinyl pyrrolidone (PVP) was dissolved in 40 mL of mixed solution (<i>V</i><sub>ethanol</sub>/<i>V</i><sub>glycerin</sub> = 1:3). Then, 0.2 g of BiCl<sub>3</sub> was completely dissolved into this solution by ultrasonic dispersion. Next, 20 mL (0.13 M in ethanol) of thiourea solution was dripped into the above solution, and this mixture was placed in a Teflon-lined autoclave and maintained at 160 °C for 14 h. After the reaction, the Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> nanorods were collected after rinsing by ethanol and deionized (DI) water before drying under 65 °C for one night with a final yield of about 260 mg.</div></div><div id="sec2_2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i5" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i5">2.2.  Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub> Fabrication</h3><div class="NLM_p last">The resulting black precipitate (50 mg) and 25 μL of tetrabutyl titanate (TBT) were added in a solution containing of 60 mL of ethanol and 25 μL of DI water. The resulting solution was subjected to a stirring process in an oil bath for 2 h at 85 °C to obtain Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>.</div></div><div id="sec2_3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i6" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i6">2.3.  Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy Fabrication</h3><div class="NLM_p last">The resulting Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub> powder (50 mg) and 17 μL of pyrrole were successively dispersed in 40 mL of DI water with stirring. After that, 5 mL of 0.1 M ammonium persulfate (APS) was added in the solution and stirred for 5 h to obtain Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy.</div></div><div id="sec2_4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i7" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i7">2.4.  Characterization</h3><div class="NLM_p">An X-ray powder diffractometer (XRD, Bruker D8 ADVANCE), a scanning electron microscope (SEM, JEOL JSM-6700F), a transmission electron microscope (TEM, JEOL JEM-2010F), a Raman spectrometer (LabRAM HR Evolution, HORIBA), X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS, Kratos), a CHNS elemental analyzer (Thermo Flash EA 1112, USA), and an inductively coupled plasma mass spectrometer (ICP–MS, Thermo Scientific) were employed for characterization.</div><div class="NLM_p last">Electrochemical measurements were performed by assembling CR2032 type coin-type cells in a glovebox filled with argon. For half cells, the anode was prepared by grinding the sample, conductive black, and polyvinylidene fluoride in a mass ratio of 8:1:1 in <i>N</i>-methylpyrrolidone (NMP), which was spread on copper foil before drying. In addition, the average loading mass of the electrode is around 0.5 mg cm<sup>–2</sup>. Sodium foil and 1.0 M NaPF<sub>6</sub> in diethylene glycol dimethyl ether were used as the counter electrode and electrolyte, respectively. The electrochemical workstation (Bio-Logic VSP) was used to record the electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) and cyclic voltammetry (CV) profiles. For the full cells, the commercial Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> (NVP) was applied as the cathode active material. The cathode was fabricated by grinding NVP, conductive black, and PVDF (7:2:1) in NMP, which was spread onto aluminum foil. The N/P ratio is about 1.2:1, and the battery capacity is determined by the anode. Moreover, the average loading mass of the cathode is around 3.5 mg cm<sup>–2</sup>. Density functional theory (DFT) calculations were conducted based on the reported method and conditions. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref25" aria-label="reference 25">(25)</a></div></div></div><div id="sec3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i8">3.  Results and Discussion</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p"><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>a depicts the synthesis diagram of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy. In the XRD pattern (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c16316/suppl_file/am1c16316_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S1</a>), all the main peaks of bare Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> and the Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy composite in the XRD patterns are indexed to orthorhombic Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> (JCPDS card no. 89-8963). Furthermore, the XRD pattern of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy was refined by employing the Rietveld method through the General Structure Analysis System (GSAS) + the EXPGUI suite. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34 ref35'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref34 ref35" aria-label="reference 34 and 35">(34,35)</a> The results give a reasonably low χ<sup>2</sup> (2.37) value based on Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> (space group of <i>Pnmb</i>), with the lattice parameters of <i>a</i> = 11.12 Å, <i>b</i> = 11.25 Å, <i>c</i> = 3.97 Å, and α = β = γ = 90°. The calculated XRD patterns have a good match with experimental data (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>b). Moreover, no characteristic peak is observed for impurities, and the absence of TiO<sub>2</sub> may be due to its amorphous nature (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c16316/suppl_file/am1c16316_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S2</a>). The existence of the coating layer of PPy was verified via the Raman spectrum in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>c, in which the peaks located at 1345.28 and 1553.78 cm<sup>–1</sup> are, respectively, assigned to the pyrrole ring and the C═C bond. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36 ref37'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref36 ref37" aria-label="reference 36 and 37">(36,37)</a> Moreover, there is a peak assigned to the <i>A</i><sub>g</sub> mode of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> at 79.86 cm<sup>–1</sup>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref38" aria-label="reference 38">(38)</a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>d shows the type IV N<sub>2</sub> adsorption/desorption isotherms, which indicate the mesoporous characteristic with a 30.32 m<sup>2</sup> g<sup>–1</sup> surface area. The average size of 11.95 nm (the inset) for the mesopore is expected to be beneficial to ionic transport and thus high-rate performance.</div><figure id="fig1" data-index="1" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 1</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c16316/asset/images/medium/am1c16316_0002.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c16316/asset/images/large/am1c16316_0002.jpeg" id="gr1" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 1. (a) Schematic diagram illustrating the design of the Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy nanoflowers, (b) XRD refinement of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy, (c) Raman spectrum, and (d) N<sub>2</sub> adsorption–desorption isotherms of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy, and the inset shows the corresponding pore size distribution and XPS spectra of (e) Bi 4f and S 2p, (f) C 1s, and (g) Ti 2p in Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c16316/asset/images/large/am1c16316_0002.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.1c16316&amp;id=fig1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">The chemical composition of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy was determined by XPS, as exhibited in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c16316/suppl_file/am1c16316_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figures S3</a> and <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>e–g. The Bi, Ti, O, S, C, and N elements are found from the survey spectrum (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c16316/suppl_file/am1c16316_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S3a</a>). In the Bi 4f XPS spectrum, two obvious peaks at 157.2 and 162.5 eV were further split into two shoulder peaks 157.9 and 163.3 eV of Bi 4f<sub>7/2</sub> and Bi 4f<sub>5/2</sub>, respectively. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref39'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref39" aria-label="reference 39">(39)</a> Moreover, the peaks at 159.9 and 160.9 eV reveal a doublet with S 2p<sub>3/2</sub> and S 2p<sub>1/2</sub> in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>e. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref40" aria-label="reference 40">(40)</a> The C 1s spectrum is shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>f. The C 1s peaks can be fitted into peaks at 284.6 (C–C bond), 285.8 (C–N bond), 286.5 (C–O bond), and 288.6 eV (C═O bond). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref41" aria-label="reference 41">(41)</a> In addition, the N 1s high-resolution spectrum only shows an amine peak located at 399.6 eV (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c16316/suppl_file/am1c16316_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S3b</a>). The C–C, C–N, and amine peaks are introduced from pyrrole, whereas the weak C–O and C═O signatures are possible due to partial oxidation during the synthetic reaction. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>g shows the spectrum of Ti 2p, in which two peaks centered at 458.9 and 464.9 eV are respectively related to Ti 2p<sub>3/2</sub> and Ti 2p<sub>1/2</sub>, indicating the existence of TiO<sub>2</sub>. Moreover, the O 1s spectrum in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c16316/suppl_file/am1c16316_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S3c</a> consists of three fitted peaks at 530.8 eV corresponding to Ti–O bonds, as well as at 531.8 and 533.4 eV associated with the C–O bond and C═O bond on account of partial oxidation. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref42" aria-label="reference 42">(42)</a> The elemental analysis was conducted to investigate the C, N, and S contents, as shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c16316/suppl_file/am1c16316_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Table S1</a>. ICP–MS was also employed to identify the Bi and Ti contents, as shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c16316/suppl_file/am1c16316_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S4</a>. By comparison and calculation, the contents of PPy and TiO<sub>2</sub> in the Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy composite are about 16.5 and 0.737%, respectively. The minimal content of TiO<sub>2</sub> is regarded to take effect on restraining the volume expansion/extraction without the obvious sacrifice of the capacity of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>.</div><div class="NLM_p">Moreover, the product morphology was characterized by SEM as shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>. The hierarchical flower-like structure of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> first fabricated via a solvothermal method is illustrated in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>a,b. The nanoflowers with a diameter of 1.5–2 μm assembled of nanorods with a diameter of 41–49 nm and a length of 0.5–1 μm. After subsequently combining with TiO<sub>2</sub> and coating with PPy shells, the as-prepared material kept the same shape with bare Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>c,d). The TEM images confirm that the polymer layer is uniformly coated on each Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> nanorod and the thickness is between 16 and 20 nm. In addition, the diameter of the Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> nanorod is about 8.7 nm (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>e,f). The HRTEM image in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>h reveals that the spacing of the lattice fringes is about 0.33 nm, reflecting the (021) plane of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>. In addition, no lattice fringe is assigned to TiO<sub>2</sub>, which also proves its amorphous nature. The images of elemental mapping certify the homogeneous distribution of C and N atoms stemmed from PPy on the surface of the composite. Besides, the O atoms are almost all around the Ti atoms, and both of them are mainly distributed around Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>, confirming the Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub> structural (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>g).</div><figure id="fig2" data-index="2" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 2</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c16316/asset/images/medium/am1c16316_0003.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c16316/asset/images/large/am1c16316_0003.jpeg" id="gr2" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 2. (a, b) SEM images of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>, (c, d) SEM images, (e, f) TEM images, (g) elemental mapping images (Ti, Bi, N, S, C, and O), and (h) HRTEM image of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c16316/asset/images/large/am1c16316_0003.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.1c16316&amp;id=fig2"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">The sodium storage performance of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy was systematically probed (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>). <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figures 3</a>a and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c16316/suppl_file/am1c16316_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">S5</a> show the CV curves of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy and bare Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> at 0.1 mV s<sup>–1</sup> within 0.01–3 V, respectively. After the initial cycle, the nearly overlapped CV curves demonstrate a higher reversibility of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy than that of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>. In the initial cathodic scan of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy, the small peak at 1.49 V is related to the intercalation of sodium ion to transfer Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>Bi<sub>2-<i>x</i></sub>S<sub>3</sub>. A strong peak at 1.09 V is attributed to the occurrence of conversion reaction as well as the generation of the film of solid electrolyte interface. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref43'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref43" aria-label="reference 43">(43)</a> In addition, this peak subsequently moved to around 0.83 V. The three close-set peaks at 0.58, 0.43, and 0.38 V might be assigned to the following multistep alloying progress of metallic Bi to form NaBi, Na<sub>2</sub>Bi, and Na<sub>3</sub>Bi, respectively. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref30" aria-label="reference 30">(30)</a> For charging scanning, the peaks located at 0.61 and 0.78 V correspond to the multistep de-alloying progresses. The peaks at 1.95 and 2.09 V reflect the reverse conversion and sodium–deintercalation reactions, respectively. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>b,c presents the rate performance and corresponding profiles of galvanostatic charge/discharge (GCD) under various current densities. The Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy composite delivered the specific capacities of 516.8, 450.5, 397.8, 355.8, 305.3, and 269.5 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at 0.2, 0.5, 1, 2, 5, and 10 A g<sup>–1</sup>, respectively. After high-rate ion intercalation/de-intercalation processes, the composite reached a capacity of 469.1 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> as the current density was set back to 0.5 A g<sup>–1</sup>. It also displays the poor rate performances of bare Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>, Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>, and Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>@PPy. For the bare Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> and Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>, it can be seen that their capacities could not recover after cycling at high current densities, suggesting that merely TiO<sub>2</sub> coating could not effectively buffer the vast volumetric variation of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> during reactions, although it does improve electrochemical performance. For the effect of PPy coating, it can make the materials, including bare Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> and Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>, more adaptable to endure the changes in current density. Further cyclic stability was studied at 5 and 10 A g<sup>–1</sup> as shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>d,e. In addition, all the electrodes underwent the active process tested under low current density for several cycles. By comparison, the Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy electrode showed the best cycle life, delivering a value of 333.9 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> over 500 cycles. The minor fluctuation in capacity may be due to large diurnal temperature difference. It can be found that the capacities of the Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy anode are lower than the bare Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> in the first several cycles<sub>,</sub> which can be attributed to the low capacities of the introduced PPy and TiO<sub>2</sub> components, as shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c16316/suppl_file/am1c16316_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S6</a>. Although the dual coating of PPy and TiO<sub>2</sub> brought down the capacity of the composite, its structural protective effect makes the Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy present good cyclic stability. The GCD and d<i>Q</i>/d<i>V</i> curves of different cycles at 5 A g<sup>–1</sup> indicates that Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy underwent a continuous activation process of about 50 cycles at the beginning, during which the sodium-ion insertion/extraction reaction gradually stabilized. The TEM images of these four samples after cycling and SEM images for Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy after cycling are shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.1c16316/suppl_file/am1c16316_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S7–S9</a> to further illustrate the effect of dual coating on structural stability. By comparison with other reported Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>-based anode materials for SIBs (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>h), this dual-structural-restrained Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy displays outstanding rate performance. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29 ref44 ref45 ref46 ref47 ref48 ref49'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref29 ref44 ref45 ref46 ref47 ref48 ref49" aria-label="reference 29 and 44 to 49">(29,44−49)</a></div><figure id="fig3" data-index="3" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 3</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c16316/asset/images/medium/am1c16316_0004.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c16316/asset/images/large/am1c16316_0004.jpeg" id="gr3" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 3. Electrochemical properties of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy: (a) CV curves; (b) rate capability compared with Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>, Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>, and Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>@PPy; (c) corresponding GCD profiles at various current densities, long-term cycling performance at (d) 5 A g<sup>–1</sup> and (e) 10 A g<sup>–1</sup> compared with Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>, Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>, and Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>@PPy; (f) GCD curves and (g) d<i>Q</i>/d<i>V</i> curves for different cycles at 5 A g<sup>–1</sup>; and (h) comparison with the previous reported Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>-based SIBs anodes.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c16316/asset/images/large/am1c16316_0004.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.1c16316&amp;id=fig3"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">To further pursue practical application of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy in SIBs, the commercial Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> was utilized to pair up with the Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy anode to assemble the full cells, which were carried out in the potential window ranging from 0.4 to 3.4 V (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>a). The full cells can easily power a display panel with nine LED bulbs in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>b, preliminarily demonstrating its applicability. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>c depicts the rate capability of the full cells, which can achieve a capacity of 141.3 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at 20 A g<sup>–1</sup>. Besides, cycling performance was studied under 5 and 10 A g<sup>–1</sup> with an active process for several cycles (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>d,e, the inset). The reversible capacity of 149.5 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> was achieved under 10 A g<sup>–1</sup> at the 2500th cycle, revealing an ultralong lifespan.</div><figure id="fig4" data-index="4" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 4</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c16316/asset/images/medium/am1c16316_0005.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c16316/asset/images/large/am1c16316_0005.jpeg" id="gr4" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 4. Electrochemical properties of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy//NVP full cells: (a) schematic diagram illustrating the configuration of the full cells, (b) nine LED bulbs lighted by the full cells, (c) rate capability and (d) corresponding GCD curves, and (e) long-term cycling performance at 5 and 10 A g<sup>–1</sup>.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c16316/asset/images/large/am1c16316_0005.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.1c16316&amp;id=fig4"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">To elucidate the reaction mechanism of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy during the ion intercalation/de-intercalation processes, in situ XRD analyses were employed on a live cell within 0.01–3 V. The diffraction peaks of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> are observed at the pristine state in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>a,b, which gradually disappeared during the discharging process. The appearance of new peaks at about 30.9° is assigned to the NaBiS<sub>2</sub> (JCPDS card no. 75-0065) phase as the product of the initial conversion reaction of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref45'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref45" aria-label="reference 45">(45)</a> And then, it gradually disappeared, accompanying with the emergence of a broad peak at 27.2°, which reflected the formation of Bi (JCPDS card no. 1-0699). Along with further discharging, the generation of NaBi (JCPDS card no. 65-8735) and then Na<sub>3</sub>Bi (JCPDS card no. 74-1161) at 32.1 and 32.9°, respectively, suggest the multistep alloying reactions of Bi metal. Within the subsequent ion removal process, the diffraction peaks of the Na<sub>3</sub>Bi phase faded away with the consecutive reappearance of NaBi, Bi, NaBiS<sub>2</sub>, and Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> phases, corresponding to the de-alloying and reverse conversion reactions, and therefore confirming the reaction reversibility for the as-prepared Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy composite. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref48'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref48" aria-label="reference 48">(48)</a> Based on the CV curves (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>c) under various scan speeds, the <i>b</i> values are determined to be 0.73 (anodic peak at 2.1 V) and 0.59 (cathodic peak at 0.35 V) (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>d), suggesting that the total stored capacity of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy is contributed by joint diffusion- and capacitive-controlled processes. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref50'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref50" aria-label="reference 50">(50)</a> In addition, the calculated ratios of capacitive contribution are shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>e. It can be found that the capacitive contribution ratio is going up along the rising of scan speed to 70% at 1.2 mV s<sup>–1</sup>. The reaction kinetic is known to be strongly associated with the transportation of sodium ion in the materials and electrons between the interface of electrolyte and electrode. Galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) and EIS measurements were applied for the exploration of the electrochemical kinetics of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy. The GITT tests were conducted at 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup> of the third cycle of various materials, as shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>f. It can be found that Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy possesses much higher values of the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficient with a stable trend compared with the other samples. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>g shows the EIS results fitted with an equivalent circuit model to explore the electrochemical kinetics. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref51'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref51" aria-label="reference 51">(51)</a> Benefitting from the Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub> heterojunction, the charge-transfer resistance (<i>R</i><sub>ct</sub>) of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub> is significantly smaller compared to that of bare Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>, which is comparable to that of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>@PPy. In addition, the <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy is further reduced by coating with the PPy layer. Thanks to the synergy between Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> and TiO<sub>2</sub>, as well as the coating of PPy, the <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy is much smaller than that of bare Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>.</div><figure id="fig5" data-index="5" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 5</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c16316/asset/images/medium/am1c16316_0006.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c16316/asset/images/large/am1c16316_0006.jpeg" id="gr5" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 5. (a) Contour map and (b) corresponding in situ XRD patterns at different states within the initial cycle of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy, (c) CV curves, (d) relationship between log <i>v</i> and log <i>i</i>, and (e) contribution rations of capacitance at various scan rates for Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy, (f) GITT and corresponding quasi-equilibrium voltage profiles of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy at 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup>, and (g) Nyquist plots of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>, Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>, Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>@PPy, and Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c16316/asset/images/large/am1c16316_0006.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.1c16316&amp;id=fig5"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">To interpret the superior electrochemical performance form the atomistic insights, calculations were employed via DFT on evaluating the effects of TiO<sub>2</sub> coating upon the structural and energy storage properties of the Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> host material using bare Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> and Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub> as prototypes for modeling. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 6</a> shows the calculated stacking structure of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub> and density of state (DOS) of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> and Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>. The charge density difference of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub> shows a gain of charge at the heterointerface between Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> and TiO<sub>2</sub>, as shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 6</a>b, which demonstrates the generation of a built-in electric field introduced by the heterojunction structure to induce accelerated charge transfer. The band gap of bare Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> was determined to be 1.34 eV, which was in agreement with the experimental value of 1.35 eV. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref52'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref52" aria-label="reference 52">(52)</a> As for Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>, the calculated band gap is 0.59 eV, much smaller than that of bare Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>, indicating that more electrons can be released into the system and in turn can increase the carrier concentration. In addition, the results are consistent with the much smaller <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub> than that of bare Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>, which were unveiled from EIS results (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>g). These consequences demonstrate that the synergistic effect between Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> and TiO<sub>2</sub> can greatly enhance the electrical conductivity and thus sodium storage property.</div><figure id="fig6" data-index="6" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 6</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c16316/asset/images/medium/am1c16316_0007.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c16316/asset/images/large/am1c16316_0007.jpeg" id="gr6" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 6. (a) Calculated stacking structures of TiO<sub>2</sub> and Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> and (b) corresponding charge density difference of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>, yellow and blue regions present the positive and negative values of electron quantities, respectively, as well as the DOS for (c) bare Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> and (d) Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.1c16316/asset/images/large/am1c16316_0007.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.1c16316&amp;id=fig6"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p last">It is concluded from the above characterization results that the pseudo-“zero-strain” TiO<sub>2</sub> coating and conductive PPy encapsulating restrain the volumetric change and maintain the structural stability to a great extent, leading to an enhancement in the cyclic stability. Although the content of TiO<sub>2</sub> is low, it carries profound implications to reinforce the electrochemical properties without sacrifice of the relatively high capacity of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>. The DFT calculations and the EIS results disclose that the build-in electric field introduced from the heterointerface of TiO<sub>2</sub> and Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> accelerates the electron transfer, which further increases electrical conductivity, and thus promotes the reaction kinetics. The merits mentioned above comprehensively contribute to the promotion in the electrochemical performance and reaction kinetics for the Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy composite.</div></div><div id="sec4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i9">4.  Conclusions</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p last">In summary, the PPy-coated Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub> nanoflowers were successfully fabricated by a facile process. The heterostructure interface between TiO<sub>2</sub> and Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> serves very well in promoting reaction kinetics and maintaining the structural integrity based on the combined effect with PPy coating. The conductive PPy layer dramatically accelerates the charge transfer to enhance the conductivity as well as suppress the massive change of the material structure. Thus, Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub>@PPy deserves to be a good candidate of the anode material, with a superior cycle life and rate capability (275.8 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> over 500 cycles at 10 A g<sup>–1</sup> in half cells and 149.5 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> over 2500 cycles at 10 A g<sup>–1</sup> in full cells). Taken as a whole, this study provides insights into the great potential of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> and the role of multiple components in the structural design for the electrode materials in the field of energy storage.</div></div><div class="NLM_back"><div class="article_supporting-info" id="notes1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div                         cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Photocatalytic Synthesis of TiO2 and Reduced Graphene Oxide Nanocomposite for Lithium Ion Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Qiu, Jingxia; Zhang, Peng; Ling, Min; Li, Sheng; Liu, Porun; Zhao, Huijun; Zhang, Shanqing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3636-3642</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this work, we synthesized graphene oxide (GO) using the improved Hummers' oxidn. method.  TiO2 nanoparticles can be anchored on the GO sheets via the abundant oxygen-contg. functional groups such as epoxy, hydroxyl, carbonyl, and carboxyl groups on the GO sheets.  Using the TiO2 photocatalyst, the GO was photocatalytically reduced under UV illumination, leading to the prodn. of TiO2-reduced graphene oxide (TiO2-RGO) nanocomposite.  The as-prepd. TiO2, TiO2-GO, and TiO2-RGO nanocomposite were used to fabricate lithium-ion batteries as the active anode materials and their corresponding lithium ion insertion/extn. performance was evaluated.  The resultant lithium-ion batteries with the TiO2-RGO nanocomposite have more stable cyclic performance, larger reversible capacity, and better rate capability, compared with that of the pure TiO2 and TiO2-GO samples.  The electrochem. and materials characterization suggest that the graphene network provides efficient pathways for electron transfer, and the TiO2 nanoparticles prevent the restacking of the graphene nanosheets, resulting in the improvement in both elec. cond. and specific capacity, resp.  This work suggests that the TiO2-based photocatalytic method could be a simple, low-cost, and efficient approach for large-scale prodn. of anode materials for lithium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGriXTyK-a0pdbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liVbwpmqLcJsg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38Xpt1Churc%253D&amp;md5=ffdf7fa7fb3c5407cacc7276b01d0c02</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref3'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit3" data-doi="10.1038/s41563-020-0729-1"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pawar, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ren, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Banerjee, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dufek, E.                         cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Glassy Li metal anode for high-performance rechargeable Li batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Xuefeng; Pawar, Gorakh; Li, Yejing; Ren, Xiaodi; Zhang, Minghao; Lu, Bingyu; Banerjee, Abhik; Liu, Ping; Dufek, Eric J.; Zhang, Ji-Guang; Xiao, Jie; Liu, Jun; Meng, Ying Shirley; Liaw, Boryann</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Materials</span>
