            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Research</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Lithium metal has been considered an ideal anode for high-energy rechargeable Li batteries, although its nucleation and growth process remains mysterious, esp. at the nanoscale.  Here, cryogenic transmission electron microscopy was used to reveal the evolving nanostructure of Li metal deposits at various transient states in the nucleation and growth process, in which a disorder-order phase transition was obsd. as a function of c.d. and deposition time.  The at. interaction over wide spatial and temporal scales was depicted by reactive mol. dynamics simulations to assist in understanding the kinetics.  Compared to cryst. Li, glassy Li outperforms in electrochem. reversibility, and it has a desired structure for high-energy rechargeable Li batteries.  Our findings correlate the crystallinity of the nuclei with the subsequent growth of the nanostructure and morphol., and provide strategies to control and shape the mesostructure of Li metal to achieve high performance in rechargeable Li batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo6f_lmtvHcWrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li74QarNCmwHQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhsVGqtLjP&amp;md5=86b6b978859de0b331c1073ca390c13b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref4'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit4" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201501666"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.                         cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nanoengineered Organic Electrodes for Highly Durable and Ultrafast Cycling of Organic Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Thangavel, Ranjith; Moorthy, Megala; Ganesan, Bala Krishnan; Lee, Wontae; Yoon, Won-Sub; Lee, Yun-Sung</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">16</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">41</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2003688</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SMALBC</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have become increasingly important as next-generation energy storage systems for application in large-scale energy storage.  It is very crucial to develop an eco-friendly and green SIB technique with superior performance for sustainable future use.  Replacing the conventional inorg. electrode materials with green and safe org. electrodes will be a promising approach.  However, the poor electrochem. kinetics, unstable electrode-electrolyte interface, high soly. of the electrodes in the electrolyte, and large amt. of conductive carbon present great challenges for org. SIBs.  In this study, the issues of org. electrodes are addressed through at.-level manipulation of these org. mols. using a series of ultrathin (Å-level) metal oxide coatings (Al2O3, ZnO, and TiO2).  Uniform and precise coatings on the perylene-3,4,9,10-tetracarboxylicacid dianhydride by gas-phase at. layer deposition technique shows a stable interphase, enhanced electrochem. kinetics (71C, 10 A g-1), and excellent stability (89%-500 cycles) compared to conventional org. electrode (70%-200 cycles).  Further studies reveal that the chem. stability of the metal oxide coating layer plays a crit. role in influencing the redox behavior, and improving kinetics of org. electrodes.  This study opens a new avenue for developing high-energy org. SIBs with performance equiv. to inorg. counterparts.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp1-kyFQ3IQorVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li74QarNCmwHQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhvFSisb%252FF&amp;md5=30676fce019406af3c66b2bacc23f721</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref6'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit6" data-doi="10.1039/c1ee01598b"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Etacheri, V.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Marom, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Elazari, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Salitra, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Aurbach, D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Challenges     in the Development of Advanced Li-Ion Batteries: A Review</span>. <i>Energy Environ.                         cas_cit6R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">6</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Challenges in the development of advanced Li-ion batteries: a review</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Etacheri, Vinodkumar; Marom, Rotem; Elazari, Ran; Salitra, Gregory; Aurbach, Doron</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Li-ion battery technol. has become very important in recent years as these batteries show great promise as power sources that can lead us to the elec. vehicle (EV) revolution.  The development of new materials for Li-ion batteries is the focus of research in prominent groups in the field of materials science throughout the world.  Li-ion batteries can be considered to be the most impressive success story of modern electrochem. in the last two decades.  They power most of today's portable devices, and seem to overcome the psychol. barriers against the use of such high energy d. devices on a larger scale for more demanding applications, such as EV.  Since this field is advancing rapidly and attracting an increasing no. of researchers, it is important to provide current and timely updates of this constantly changing technol.  In this review, we describe the key aspects of Li-ion batteries: the basic science behind their operation, the most relevant components, anodes, cathodes, electrolyte solns., as well as important future directions for R&amp;D of advanced Li-ion batteries for demanding use, such as EV and load-leveling applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpS5wrQXqBLLbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li74QarNCmwHQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXht1Cqs7jE&amp;md5=74c50c1f50dfffe2bb90d8e3aae4f157</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref7'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit7" data-doi="10.1126/science.276.5317.1395"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Idota, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kubota, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mutsufuji, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Maekawa, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Miyasaka, T.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Tin-Based Amorphous Oxide: A High-Capacity Lithium-Ion-Storage Material</span>. <i>Science</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">1997</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>276</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1395</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1397</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit7R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">7</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Tin-based amorphous oxide: a high-capacity lithium-ion-storage material</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Idota, Yoshio; Kubota, Tadahiko; Matsufuji, Akihiro; Maekawa, Yukio; Miyasaka, Tsutomu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Science (Washington, D.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A high-capacity lithium-storage material in metal-oxide form has been synthesized that can replace the carbon-based lithium intercalation materials currently in extensive use as the neg. electrode (anode) of lithium-ion rechargeable batteries.  This tin-based amorphous composite oxide (TCO) contains Sn(II)-O as the active center for lithium insertion and other glass-forming elements, which make up an oxide network.  The TCO anode yields a specific capacity for reversible lithium adsorption more than 50 percent higher than those of the carbon families that persists after charge-discharge cyclin when coupled with a lithium cobalt oxide cathode.  Lithium-7 NMR measurements evidenced the high ionic state of Li retained in the charged state, in which TCO accepted 8 mol of lithium ions per unit mole.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrTzO7h-e5WZbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li74QarNCmwHQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADyaK2sXjsFKqt7o%253D&amp;md5=48667ff9c768880afd28a5e6fa24ddd9</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref8'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit8" data-doi="10.1016/j.mattod.2020.04.004"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pollard, T.                         cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrolyte design for Li metal-free Li batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Ji; Li, Qin; Pollard, Travis P.; Fan, Xiulin; Borodin, Oleg; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Materials Today (Oxford, United Kingdom)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">39</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">118-126</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">MTOUAN</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1369-7021</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Here, we use a lithiophilic Bismuth graphite blend (Bi-Gr) substrate to replace lithiophobic Cu current collector to seed a uniform Li nucleation, and form a lithiophobic LiF-rich SEI rather than lithiophilic org.-rich SEI to suppress Li dendrite growth.  Mol. dynamics simulations reveal the preferential redn. of anions in 2.0 M LiPF6 in tetrahydrofuran/2-Me THF (2.0 M LiPF6-mixTHF) electrolyte to generate LiF-rich SEI on plated Li.  Bi-Gr substrate and 2.0 M LiPF6-mixTHF electrolyte enable the Li anodes to achieve a record high CE of 99.83% at a high capacity of 1.0 mAh cm-2 and current of 0.5 mA cm-2.  The Bi particles serve as dispersed nucleation centers that promote uniform Li deposition with strong adhesion to the substrate to avoid dead Li, while the lithiophobic LiF-rich SEI promotes lateral Li growth and suppresses the vertical Li dendrite growth even at a high c.d. of 3.0 mA cm-2 and high areal capacities of 3.0 mAh cm-2.  The regulation of Li nucleation and growth enables the Li metal-free LiFePO4 full cells to achieve 100 cycles at a practical areal capacity of &gt;2.0 mAh cm-2.  This manuscript highlights the benefits of simultaneous substrate design to improve Li nucleation and electrolyte design to promote lithiophobic SEI growth, enabling a promising and practical route Li metal-free Li metal batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo-ftqL6wNyZ7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgocEn83nrLLA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXnsFWqurY%253D&amp;md5=e4e398c8ba365e944eb8dfc30c9d802b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref9"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref9'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">9</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit9" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201905632"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pang, W.                         cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Coupling Topological Insulator SnSb2Te4 Nanodots with Highly Doped Graphene for High-Rate Energy Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Zhibin; Liang, Gemeng; Pang, Wei Kong; Zhou, Tengfei; Cheng, Zhenxiang; Zhang, Wenchao; Liu, Ye; Johannessen, Bernt; Guo, Zaiping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Topol. insulators have spurred worldwide interest, but their advantageous properties have scarcely been explored in terms of electrochem. energy storage, and their high-rate capability and long-term cycling stability still remain a significant challenge to harvest. p-Type topol. insulator SnSb2Te4 nanodots anchoring on few-layered graphene (SnSb2Te4/G) are synthesized as a stable anode for high-rate lithium-ion batteries and potassium-ion batteries through a ball-milling method.  These SnSb2Te4/G composite electrodes show ultralong cycle lifespan (478 mAh g-1 at 1 A g-1 after 1000 cycles) and excellent rate capability (remaining 373 mAh g-1 even at 10 A g-1) in Li-ion storage owing to the rapid ion transport accelerated by the PN heterojunction, virtual electron highways provided by the conductive topol. surface state, and extraordinary pseudocapacitive contribution, whose excellent phase reversibility is confirmed by synchrotron in situ X-ray powder diffraction.  Surprisingly, durable lifespan even at practical levels of mass loading (&gt;10 mg cm-2) for Li-ion storage and excellent K-ion storage performance are also obsd.  This work provides new insights for designing high-rate electrode materials by boosting conductive topol. surfaces, at. doping, and the interface interaction.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoaILmMSVC8z7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgocEn83nrLLA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXit1OktbjN&amp;md5=69f158327e5341cbb484b36505457251</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit10" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201703028"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tai, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sencadas, V.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Konstantinov, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.                         cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Highly Efficient Sodium Storage in Iron Oxide Nanotube Arrays Enabled by Built-In Electric Field</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ni, Jiangfeng; Sun, Menglei; Li, Liang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">High-power Na-ion batteries capable of charging and discharging rapidly and durably are eagerly demanded to replace current Li-ion batteries.  However, poor activity and instable cycling of common Na anode materials represent a huge barrier for practical deployment.  A smart design of ordered nanotube arrays of Fe2O3 is presented as efficient Na anode, simply enabled by surface sulfurization.  The resulted heterostructure of oxide and sulfide spontaneously develops a built-in elec. field, which reduces the activation energy and accelerates charge transport significantly.  Benefiting from the synergy of ordered architecture and built-in elec. field, such arrays exhibit a large reversible capacity, a superior rate capability, and a high retention of 91% up to 200 cycles at a high rate of 5 A/g, outperforming most reported Fe oxide electrodes.  Full cells based on the Fe2O3 array anode and the Na0.67(Mn0.67Ni0.23Mg0.1)O2 cathode deliver a specific energy of 142 Wh/Kg at a power d. of 330 W/Kg (based on both active electrodes), demonstrating a great potential in practical application.  This material design may open a new door in engineering efficient anode based on earth-abundant materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpq6EENu8xwvrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgocEn83nrLLA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhs12jtbbF&amp;md5=11f3028a8acb4d0a9f5bed54b715c7cc</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit12" data-doi="10.1038/nchem.2085"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Larcher, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tarascon, J.-M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Towards Greener and More Sustainable Batteries for Electrical Energy Storage</span>. <i>Nat.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Ever-growing energy needs and depleting fossil-fuel resources demand the pursuit of sustainable energy alternatives, including both renewable energy sources and sustainable storage technologies.  It is therefore essential to incorporate material abundance, eco-efficient synthetic processes and life-cycle anal. into the design of new electrochem. storage systems.  At present, a few existing technologies address these issues, but in each case, fundamental and technol. hurdles remain to be overcome.  Here the authors provide an overview of the current state of energy storage from a sustainability perspective.  The authors introduce the notion of sustainability through discussion of the energy and environmental costs of state-of-the-art Li-ion batteries, considering elemental abundance, toxicity, synthetic methods and scalability.  With the same themes in mind, the authors also highlight current and future electrochem. storage systems beyond Li-ion batteries.  The complexity and importance of recycling battery materials is also discussed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGph4-d2B3Q8DLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgocEn83nrLLA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvFKlsrjF&amp;md5=977f0fc171bb41af30457715fc0ded72</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit13" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201605820"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Confined Amorphous Red Phosphorus in MOF-Derived N-Doped Microporous Carbon as a Superior Anode for Sodium-Ion Battery</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A Practical High-Energy Cathode for Sodium-Ion Batteries Based on Uniform P2-Na0.7CoO2 Microspheres</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Fang, Yongjin; Yu, Xin-Yao; Lou, Xiong Wen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Layered metal oxides have attracted increasing attention as cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  However, the application of such cathode materials is still hindered by their poor rate capability and cycling stability.  Here, a facile self-templated strategy is developed to synthesize uniform P2-Na0.7CoO2 microspheres.  Due to the unique microsphere structure, the contact area of the active material with electrolyte is minimized.                         cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Encapsulation of NiO nanoparticles in mesoporous carbon nanospheres for advanced energy storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Mingxian; Wang, Xin; Zhu, Dazhang; Li, Liangchun; Duan, Hui; Xu, Zijie; Wang, Zhiwei; Gan, Lihua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">308</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">240-247</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMEJAJ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1385-8947</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A facile encapsulation of NiO nanoparticles in mesoporous carbon nanospheres (NiO/MCNs) is demonstrated.  Silicate-ion groups on nanosilica surface can react with Ni2+ ions to generate nickel silicate in situ around the SiO2 cores.  Such hybrids are introduced into polymer nanospheres prepd. by extended Stober strategy, followed by calcination and template removal to fabricate NiO/MCNs.  The typical NiO/MCNs have spherical morphol. (∼280 nm in diam.), uniform mesopores (5.9 nm), high sp. surface area (714 m2 g-1), and well-dispersed NiO nanoparticles (7.20 wt.%).  Package mesoporosity among the carbon spheres reduces ion diffusion distance, and the mesopores benefit fast ion transportation.  Besides, the introduction of NiO nanoparticles not only provides pseudocapacitance, but also increases the graphitization degree of the carbons and improves cryst. structure.  As a result, NiO/MCNs as supercapacitor electrodes show a high specific capacitance of 406 F g-1 at 1.0 A g-1 in 6 M KOH electrolyte, and it still maintains 315 F g-1 at a high loading c.d. of 20.0 A g-1.  Besides, NiO/MCN electrode retains ∼91.0% of the original capacity at 3.0 A g-1 after 10,000 cycles, exhibiting outstanding cycle stability.  The easy prepd., well-structured, and high-performance NiO/MCNs provide great potential to support advanced energy storage systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpk_WMZwdRiKrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljSEWSu3SVDnQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhsFOnu77N&amp;md5=9bb2393a240d65ee938cbb69f8d845d1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201900710"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pham, D.                         cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A Versatile Pyramidal Hauerite Anode in Congeniality Diglyme-Based Electrolytes for Boosting Performance of Li- and Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Pham, Duong Tung; Vu, Trang Thi; Kim, Sungjin; Sambandam, Balaji; Mathew, Vinod; Lim, Jinsub; Kim, Jaekook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">For the first time, environmentally friendly sulfur-rich pyramidal MnS2 synthesized via a single-step hydrothermal process is used as a high-performance anode material in Li-ion and Na-ion batteries.  The superior electrochem. performance of the MnS2 electrode along with its high compatibility with ether-based electrolytes are analyzed in both half- and full-cell configurations.  The reversible capacities of ≈84 mAh g-1 and ≈74 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 50 mA g-1 are retained in the Li-ion and Na-ion full-cells, resp., over 200 cycles with excellent capacity retentions.                         cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Novel one-step gas-phase reaction synthesis of transition metal sulfide nanoparticles embedded in carbon matrices for reversible lithium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lou, Peili; Tan, Yingbin; Lu, Ping; Cui, Zhonghui; Guo, Xiangxin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">This report presents a novel one-step method based on the gas-phase reaction between metallocenes and sulfur for synthesizing the nanocomposites of transition metal sulfide nanoparticles embedded in carbon matrixes (TMS@C).  Various nanocomposites including FeS@C, Cr2S3@C and NiS2@C have been successfully synthesized by using ferrocene, chromocene and nickelocene, resp.  The SEM investigations evidence that the TMS nanoparticles are evenly distributed in the in situ formed carbon matrixes, demonstrating that this novel method is an easy way to synthesize homogeneous TMS-based nanocomposites with well-controlled nanostructures.  As the anodes for lithium ion batteries (LIBs), the as-prepd. TMS@C electrodes exhibit excellent rate capability and high reversible capacity.  For example, a high reversible capacity of 550 and 480 mA h g-1 can be retained for the FeS@C anode even after 350 cycles at a c.d. of 0.1 A g-1 and 500 cycles at 0.5 A g-1, resp.  The TEM investigations on the 100th discharged and recharged electrodes demonstrate superior structural stability against repeated lithiation/delithiation of the FeS@C.  These impressive results indicate that this novel approach is a promising way to synthesize high-performance TMS electrodes for highly reversible lithium storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpdTtVYsXxsCLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljSEWSu3SVDnQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xhtlyqt7rM&amp;md5=e90101979cf06bca2157bf39261ef479</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201700488"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.                         cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sb2S3-Bi2S3 microrods with the combined action of carbon encapsulation and rGO confinement for improving high cycle stability in sodium/potassium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Kai; Liu, Xiaofeng; Qin, Yanchao; Zhao, Zhipeng; Xu, Yanan; Yi, Yuhao; Guan, Hui; Fu, Yinghua; Liu, Pu; Li, Dan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">For sodium and potassium storage, the inevitably large vol. variation in the process of charge/discharge for the anode materials with conversion and alloying mechanisms leads to unsatisfactory structural stability and capacity retention.                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Rapidly Synthesized, Few-Layered Pseudocapacitive SnS2 Anode for High-Power Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Thangavel, Ranjith; Samuthira Pandian, Amaresh; Ramasamy, Hari Vignesh; Lee, Yun-Sung</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The abundance of sodium resources has recently motivated the investigation of sodium ion batteries (SIBs) as an alternative to com. lithium ion batteries.  However, the low power and low capacity of conventional sodium anodes hinder their practical realization.  Although most research has concd. on the development of high-capacity sodium anodes, anodes with a combination of high power and high capacity have not been widely realized.  Herein, we present a simple microwave irradn. technique for obtaining few-layered, ultrathin two-dimensional SnS2 over graphene sheets in a few minutes.  SnS2 possesses a large no. of active surface sites and exhibits high-capacity, rapid sodium ion storage kinetics induced by quick, nondestructive pseudocapacitance.  Enhanced sodium ion storage at a high c.d. (12 A g-1), accompanied by high reversibility and high stability, was demonstrated.  Addnl., a rationally designed sodium ion full cell coupled with SnS2//Na3V2(PO4)3 exhibited exceptional performance with high initial Coulombic efficiency (99%), high capacity, high stability, and a retention of ∼53% of the initial capacity even after the c.d. was increased by a factor of 140.  In addn., a high specific energy of ∼140 Wh kg-1 and an ultrahigh specific power of ∼8.3 kW kg-1 (based on the mass of both the anode and cathode) were obsd.  Because of its outstanding performance and rapid synthesis, few-layered SnS2 could be a promising candidate for practical realization of high-power SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrGRiDOPGxr67Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lglym11NlbMZA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhslags77F&amp;md5=b0d6b6a8322c73803b08e14a8891aae0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit21" data-doi="10.1002/smll.201900258"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Braun, P.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Low energy d. is the key issue that needs to be addressed for sodium ion batteries.  Antimony sulfide (Sb2S3) with high theor. capacity is considered as an ideal anode, but it suffers from poor electrochem. activity and consequently, low energy d.  Simple hollow Sb2S3 structures with high electrochem. activity offer high gravimetric energy d., while large internal voids significantly decrease the volumetric energy d.  Here, multi-shell Sb2S3 was synthesized as an anode for sodium ion batteries, exhibiting much higher reversible capacity and gravimetric energy d. than the pristine Sb2S3.  Moreover, the multi-shell structure presents higher volumetric energy d. with enhanced durability than its single-shell counterpart due to the optimized utilization of the inner void.  Operando synchrotron-based X-ray powder diffraction (XRPD) was used to verify the enhanced electrochem. activity originated from more complete conversion electrochem. reactions.  The multi-shell Sb2S3 design may provide a guide for the development of high-performance hollow structured anodes with preserved high energy d.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqkS3XWnf8CPLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lglym11NlbMZA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXnt1Sqtbc%253D&amp;md5=81f6b5d6332cfc56ba64f41e2bc7d4be</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit23" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.9b06161"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Šiškins, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Alijani, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">van Blankenstein, M.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Two-dimensional (2D) materials with strong in-plane anisotropy are of interest for enabling orientation-dependent, frequency-tunable, optomech. devices.  However, black phosphorus (bP), the 2D material with the largest anisotropy to date, is unstable as it degrades in air.  In this work we show that As2S3 is an interesting alternative, with a similar anisotropy to bP, while at the same time having a much higher chem. stability.  We probe the mech. and optical anisotropy in As2S3 by three distinct angular-resolved exptl. methods: Raman spectroscopy, at. force microscopy (AFM), and resonance frequency anal.  Using a dedicated angle-resolved AFM force-deflection method, an in-plane anisotropy factor of (Ea/Ec) = 1.7 is found in the Young's modulus of As2S3 with Ea-axis = 79.1 ± 10.1 GPa and Ec-axis = 47.2 ± 7.9 GPa.                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchical self-assembled Bi2S3 hollow nanotubes coated with sulfur-doped amorphous carbon as advanced anode materials for lithium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dong, Yucheng; Hu, Mingjun; Zhang, Zhenyu; Zapien, Juan Antonio; Wang, Xin; Lee, Jong-Min</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Bismuth sulfide (Bi2S3) is considered as a promising anode material for lithium ion batteries (LIBs) owing to its high theor. specific capacity and intriguing reaction mechanism.  However, capacity fading and cycling instability due to vol. variation during the lithiation/delithiation process still remain a great challenge.  Herein, we proposed a simple glucose assisted hydrothermal strategy and followed a post-treatment process to prep. hierarchical sulfur-doped carbon Bi2S3 (Bi2S3@SC) hollow nanotubes that self-assembled into sulfur-doped amorphous carbon coated Bi2S3 nanocrystals as building blocks.  Glucose plays a decisive role in the formation process of Bi2S3 nanocrystals and subsequent self-assembly, forming Bi2S3@SC hollow nanotubes.  The polysaccharide shell formed on the surface of Bi2S3 nanocrystals during the hydrothermal process was transformed into the sulfur-doped amorphous carbon layer after the post-treatment process.  Electrochem. tests reveal that the resulting composites exhibit excellent electrochem. performance with a highly reversible cycling capacity of ∼950 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1, as well as a good rate capability and significantly enhanced cycling stability derived from their unique structural features, thus demonstrating the potential of Bi2S3@SC hollow nanotubes as high performance anode materials for LIBs. Optical absorption expts. revealed that the Bi2S3 nanowires are narrow-band semiconductors with a band gap Eg ≈ 1.33 eV.  Elec. transport measurements on individual nanowires gave a resistivity of about 1.2 Ω cm and an emission current of 3.5 μA at a bias field of 35 V/μm.  This current corresponds to a c.d. of about 105 A/cm2, which makes the Bi2S3 nanowire a potential candidate for applications in field-emission electronic devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrrKt-f1Dx-frVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgdwa6QY0OrCA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD2MXhtVWnu7%252FK&amp;md5=eeb8da147784d6b9baf3ed030ea5d033</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1021/ja0284512"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ye, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Meng, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Rational Growth of Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> Nanotubes from Quasi-Two-Dimensional Precursors</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Heterointerface Engineering of Hierarchical Bi2S3/MoS2 with Self-Generated Rich Phase Boundaries for Superior Sodium Storage Performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cao, Liang; Liang, Xinghui; Ou, Xing; Yang, Xianfeng; Li, Yangzhong; Yang, Chenghao; Lin, Zhang; Liu, Meilin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Regulating nanocrystal compn. with multiphase compds. is considered an efficient approach to enhance electrochem. performance and structure stability.  Nevertheless, the thorough understanding of significant reaction mechanisms and insight into the reason of enhanced performance is still urgent.  In this work, the bimetallic sulfide Bi2S3/MoS2 heterogeneous with abundant phase boundaries is successfully fabricated.  The in situ investigation of Na+-storage mechanism confirms that enormous phase boundaries are self-generated by compn. optimization and rational structural design.  More importantly, the full understanding of abundant phase boundaries on the enhanced electrochem. properties is explicitly unraveled by combining theor. anal. and exptl. results.  It confirms that the interior self-built-in elec.-field induced by phase boundaries can enhance the reaction kinetics and boost the charge transfer.  Besides, the Bi/Na2S interface is well-maintained by the homogeneously distributed phase boundaries, effectively improving the conversion/alloying reversibility and keeping integrity without agglomeration and pulverization.  As expected, the Bi2S3/MoS2 composite exhibits superior rate capability and long-cycling stability (323.4 mAh g-1 after long-term 1200 cycles at ultrahigh rate of 10 A g-1).  This strategy of constructing sufficient phase boundaries sheds light on the enhancement of reversibility and stability for other advanced conversion/alloying-type anode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrNEP3nN2QDfrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgdwa6QY0OrCA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXjslyisLg%253D&amp;md5=ca12b7d930feff4752873f6961f7aa4a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit31" data-doi="10.1016/j.jechem.2020.11.007"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cai, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cui, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhan, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> Spheres     Coated with MOF-Derived Co<sub>9</sub>S<sub>8</sub> and N-Doped Carbon Composite Layer for     Half/Full Sodium-Ion Batteries with Superior Performance</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High Volumetric Quasi-Solid-State Sodium-Ion Capacitor under High Mass Loading Conditions</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Thangavel, Ranjith; Kannan, Aravindaraj G.; Ponraj, Rubha; Park, Myung-Soo; Choi, Hwan; Kim, Dong-Won; Lee, Yun-Sung</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">19</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The sodium-ion capacitor (NIC) represents an important research approach to bridge the gap between batteries and capacitors, but is still limited by inferior energy behavior at high power, low volumetric performance, low electrode mass loading, and safety issues with conventional liq. electrolyte.  Herein, a high-performing, kinetically superior, and safer quasi-solid-state NIC utilizing the fast sodium storage in TiO2 and rapid ion adsorption on a biomass-derived porous carbon with a sodium-ion conducting P(VDF-HFP) gel polymer electrolyte is presented.  Owing to high mass loading, low graphene content in TiO2, and by overcoming the diffusion-limited sodium storage by surface limited storage enable the NIC to deliver an impressive volumetric energy of ≈89 Wh L-1 (94 Wh kg-1) based on total mass in both electrodes.  Also, a remarkable power of ≈9.4 kW L-1 (10 kW kg-1) while retaining an energy of ≈28.7 Wh L-1 (30.6 Wh kg-1) is attained.  Furthermore, the NIC shows a long-term stability both at room temp. and high temp. (50°C), outperforming conventional NICs.  This research opens new opportunities for applications of high-performing and safer NICs in next-generation storage devices requiring high energy at high power with high safety.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqRvYAITQ4IjbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liJBrpmlBC4sA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhvVOiur%252FO&amp;md5=b56b5e2c6fa6c83b68e13d1d1aacd8cd</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2016.08.115"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qiu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Effects of PPy, GO and PPy/GO Composites on The Negative Plate and on The High-Rate Partial-State-Of-Charge     Performance of Lead-Acid Batteries</span>. <i>Electrochim.         </div><div class="casAbstract">To improve the high-rate partial-state-of-charge (HRPSoC) performance of Pb-acid batteries for hybrid-elec. vehicles, graphene oxide (GO), polypyrrole (PPy) and three PPy/GO composites with different wt. ratio of pyrrole to GO (mpy/mGO) were selected as additives to form neg. plates and simulated test cells.  The effects of these additives on the electrochem. performance and the microstructure of the neg. plate and on the HRPSoC cycle performance of the simulated test cell were studied.  The microstructure of the neg. plate is changed with the addn. of different additives.  GO significantly increases the H (H2) evolution ability of the neg. plate, while PPy has the opposite effect.  The incorporation of the proper content of PPy with GO can effectively inhibit the H2 evolution of the neg. plate.  Also, adding different additives in the neg. plate also decreases its total impedance, accelerates the redox processes between Pb and PbSO4 on it and increases its specific capacitance.  GO and the PPy/GO composite with mpy/mGO = 1:1 (PG1) can significantly increase the HRPSoC cycle life of the simulated test cell.  Considering the H2 evolution performance and the HRPSoC cycle performance, the PPy/GO composites with a medium mpy/mGO ratio, such as PG1, may be the appropriate additives for the neg. plate of Pb-acid batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo8-jOSZFFETLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liJBrpmlBC4sA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhsVegt7vO&amp;md5=ee576f2e9810ab1679d80239d2328dbc</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1107/s0021889801002242"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Toby, B.                         cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">In situ hydrothermal deposition as an efficient catalyst supporting method towards low-temperature graphitization of amorphous carbon</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xie, Mingjiang; Yang, Jie; Liang, Jiyuan; Guo, Xuefeng; Ding, Weiping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">In view of the fact that the catalytic activity of supported catalyst is greatly influenced by its impregnation method, an in situ hydrothermal deposition method was explored and applied to load iron catalyst onto the amorphous carbon matrix, which derived from a soft-templating method with sucrose as precursor, to prep. nanoporous graphitic carbon at low temp.  Compared to traditional impregnation method, this hydrothermal loading method could realize the phase transformation from amorphous carbon to graphitic carbon at a temp. as low as 650 °C.  Systematic studies on the hydrothermal deposition and catalytic graphitization were made by X-ray diffraction and Raman spectrum, indicating that hydrothermal impregnation temp. and duration are the two crucial factors to the catalytic performance of loaded iron oxide.  The obtained graphitic carbon by this approach possesses a nanoporous structure with surface area up to 329 m2/g, pore vol. of 0.39 cm3/g and achieves a capacitance per unit surface area of 39.5 μF/cm2, much higher than that of the carbon derived from traditional impregnation method (24.6 μF/cm2).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpC-ke3AnVybLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liJBrpmlBC4sA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Polypyrrole-encapsulated amorphous Bi2S3 hollow sphere for long life sodium ion batteries and lithium-sulfur batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Long, Bei; Qiao, Zhengping; Zhang, Jingnan; Zhang, Shanqing; Balogun, Muhammad-Sadeeq; Lu, Jun; Song, Shuqin; Tong, Yexiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">18</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11370-11378</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium ion batteries (SIBs) and lithium-sulfur (Li-S) batteries are considered as the most promising next-generation energy storage devices to displace the widely used lithium ion batteries due to their inherent advantages.  Here, polypyrrole-encapsulated amorphous Bi2S3 hollow spheres are prepd. by the sulfuration of Bi-glycol spheres with a polypyrrole (PPy) coating.  Benefiting from the unique hollow structure (Kirkendall effect) and the excellent cond. and flexibility of the PPy coating, this material can be applied in both SIBs and Li-S batteries.  For SIBs, the unconductive amorphous Bi2S3 is electrochem. reduced to conductive metallic Bi, leading to a Bi-PPy core-shell structure.  The resulting Bi acts as the main active material while the PPy coating accommodates the vol. variation of Bi during sodiation/desodiation.  For Li-S batteries, the outer double layer structure effectively prevents the dissoln. and "shuttle effect" of polysulfides by phys. contg. and chem. adsorbing polysulfides, and tolerates the vol. expansion of sulfur.  Meanwhile, the residual polyvinyl pyrrolidone in the prepn. process is chem. bonded with sulfur and exhibits the electrochem. properties, and results in addnl. discharging/charging capacity.  Thus, this multifunctional electrode shows excellent rate capability and cycling life in SIBs and Li-S batteries.  This work provides new insight into the design of multifunctional electrodes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpBUttb3gdkQrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhgtFd1mt5c4Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXks12msrY%253D&amp;md5=d0cc2b10bd0dbd3d447f88d82394ceb6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref39'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit39" data-doi="10.1016/j.jphotochem.2020.113060"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jin, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guan, Z.-C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.-P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, G.-K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Du, R.-G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>/rGO Co-Modified TiO<sub>2</sub> Nanotube Photoanode for Enhanced Photoelectrochemical Cathodic     Protection of Stainless Steel</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel Bi2S3/reduced graphene oxide (rGO) co-modified TiO2 nanotube photoanode was fabricated on a Ti foil by anodization combined with cyclic voltammetric electrodeposition, and successive ionic layer adsorption and reaction. Under white light irradn., the composite film in a 0.1 M Na2SO3 and 0.1 M Na2S soln. exhibited 62.5 times higher photocurrent d. than the TiO2 film.                 10.1016/j.nanoen.2017.01.033</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D33%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D213-220%26journal%3DNano%2BEnergy%26author%3DH.%2BLiang%26author%3DJ.%2BNi%26author%3DL.%2BLi%26title%3DBio-Inspired%2BEngineering%2Bof%2BBi2S3-PPy%2BYolk-Shell%2BComposite%2Bfor%2BHighly%2BDurable%2BLithium%2Band%2BSodium%2B%2B%2B%2B%2BStorage%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.nanoen.2017.01.033&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c16316&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.nanoen.2017.01.033&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Bio-inspired engineering of Bi2S3-PPy yolk-shell composite for highly durable lithium and sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liang, Haichen; Ni, Jiangfeng; Li, Liang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">33</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">213-220</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Bismuth based compds. are uniquely interesting as anode materials in energy storage devices such as rechargeable batteries, owing to their large volumetric capacity and suitable operating potential higher than graphite.  How to achieve the high capacity durably and robustly remains an open challenge.  To address this issue, here we propose a bio-inspired material engineering of yolk-shell composite that consists of bismuth sulfide (Bi2S3) nanowire assembly intimately encapsulated in polypyrrole (PPy) shell.  The Bi2S3 yolk features a large void space and a short diffusion distance, while the PPy shell is highly conductive, flexible and resilient, allowing for the free vol. variation upon ion uptake and release.  When used as anode, the Bi2S3-PPy yolk-shell composite exhibits a superior Li storage cyclability (99% for 500 cycles) and a high rate capability (337 mAh g-1 at 10 C), outstripping any previous bismuth based materials.  This composite also affords a high reversible capacity of 591 mAh g-1 and a favorable durability for Na storage.  The discrepancy between Li and Na storage may correlate to the larger vol. change of Bi alloying with Na (∼250%) against with Li (∼110%).  This work offers a potential creative approach to engineering efficient electrodes for energy storage applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGovto5xM8CXa7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhgtFd1mt5c4Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXit1Squ7Y%253D&amp;md5=949f4f32dff24a1486a9f12104b2d489</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1039/c9nj04581c"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jin, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ju, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wen, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Q.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">MOF-Derived NiO-NiCo<sub>2</sub>O<sub>4</sub>@PPy Hollow     Polyhedron as a Sulfur Immobilizer for Lithium-Sulfur Batteries</span>. <i>New J.                         cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">MOF-derived NiO-NiCo2O4@PPy hollow polyhedron as a sulfur immobilizer for lithium-sulfur batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu, Fengchao; Jin, Bo; Li, Huan; Ju, Wentao; Wen, Zi; Jiang, Qing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">New Journal of Chemistry</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The lithium-sulfur battery has been regarded as a highly competitive candidate for the efficient energy storage devices owing to its high theor. capacity (1675 mA h g-1) and energy d. (2600 W h kg-1).  Herein, a unique metal-org. framework (MOF)-derived NiO-NiCo2O4@PPy hollow polyhedral structure material is designed and synthesized as an efficient sulfur immobilizer for lithium-sulfur batteries (LSBs).  The NiO-NiCo2O4@PPy structure effectively alleviates vol. expansion, increases electronic cond., and enhances the binding effect on lithium polysulfides by chem. fixation.  The S/NiO-NiCo2O4@PPy composite displays a high initial discharge capacity of 963 mA h g-1 with a high initial coulombic efficiency of 95.2% at a low c.d. of 0.2C.  In addn., this sample exhibits good cycling performance at a high c.d. of 1C.  All the results show that this design strategy has great potential to promote the design of MOF-derived materials for LSBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoHCur9Ikuf37Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhgtFd1mt5c4Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhvF2gur3O&amp;md5=48099536001d74a1d9358db3443a514a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit42" data-doi="10.1021/jp9639399"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Södergren, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Seigbahn, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rensmo, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lindström, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hagfeldt, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lindquist, S.-E.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Lithium Intercalation in Nanoporous Anatase TiO<sub>2</sub> Studied with XPS</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Synthesis of Bi2S3/C yolk-shell composite based on sulfur impregnation for efficient sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Hyeongwoo; Kim, Dowon; Lee, Yongho; Byun, Dongjin; Kim, Hyung-Seok; Choi, Wonchang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">383</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">123094</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMEJAJ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1385-8947</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Bismuth sulfide (Bi2S3) is considered as an attractive anode material for sodium-ion battery (SIB) systems owing to its high theor. capacity (625 mAh g-1) and laminar structure for storing host ions.  However, capacity fading due to the large vol. change during long term cycling is a serious problem preventing the practical application of this material to SIBs.  Also, its elec. cond. is still unsatisfactory.  To solve those problems, the design of a Bi2S3/C composite with a yolk-shell type structure is proposed.  The synthesis method of Bi2S3/C yolk-shell composite includes the fabrication of Bi/C yolk-shell platforms followed by a simple sulfur-impregnation step to obtain Bi2S3/C yolk-shell composites.  This sulfur-impregnation step does not result in any degrdn. of the particle structure and preserves the uniform carbon shell.  Furthermore, the Bi2S3/C yolks-shell composite displays enhanced electrochem. performance as an SIB anode material and exhibits high stability during long-term cycling (282.4 mAh g-1 after 300 cycles at 0.2C) and improved rate capability (413.0 mAh g-1 at 10C).  These improvements are mainly attributed to the conductive electron pathway provided by the carbon shell and the suppression of large vol. changes due to the presence of voids in the yolk-shell structure.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrsGoJiLo8K0rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhgtFd1mt5c4Q"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nanostructured Bi2S3 encapsulated within three-dimensional N-doped graphene as active and flexible anodes for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lu, Chen; Li, Zhenzhu; Yu, Lianghao; Zhang, Li; Xia, Zhou; Jiang, Tao; Yin, Wanjian; Dou, Shixue; Liu, Zhongfan; Sun, Jingyu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4614-4626</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NRAEB5</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Springer GmbH</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have been increasingly attracting attention as a sustainable alternative to lithium-ion batteries for scalable energy storage.  The key to advanced SIBs relies heavily upon the development of reliable anodes.  In this respect, Bi2S3 has been extensively investigated because of its high capacity, tailorable morphol., and low cost.  However, the common practices of incorporating carbon species to enhance the elec. cond. and accommodate the vol. change of Bi2S3 anodes so as to boost their durability for Na storage have met with limited success.  Herein, we report a simple method to realize the encap sulation of Bi2S3 nanorods within three-dimensional, nitrogen-doped graphene (3DNG) frameworks, targeting flexible and active composite anodes for SIBs.  The Bi2S3/3DNG composites displayed outstanding Na storage behavior with a high reversible capacity (649 mAh·g-1 at 62.5 mA·g-1) and favorable durability (307 and 200 mAh·g-1 after 100 cycles at 125 and 312.5 mA·g-1, resp.).  In-depth characterization by in situ X-ray diffraction revealed that the intriguing Na storage process of Bi2S3 was based upon a reversible reaction.  Furthermore, a full, flexible SIB cell with Na0.4MnO2 cathode and as-prepd. composite anode was successfully assembled, and holds a great promise for next-generation, wearable energy storage applications.                         cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Heterostructured Bi2S3-Bi2O3 Nanosheets with a Built-In Electric Field for Improved Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Luo, Wen; Li, Feng; Li, Qidong; Wang, Xuanpeng; Yang, Wei; Zhou, Liang; Mai, Liqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Constructing novel heterostructures has great potential in tuning the phys./chem. properties of functional materials for electronics, catalysis, as well as energy conversion and storage.  In this work, heterostructured Bi2S3-Bi2O3 nanosheets (BS-BO) have been prepd. through an easy water-bath approach.  The formation of such unique BS-BO heterostructures was achieved through a controllable thioacetamide-directed surfactant-assisted reaction process.  Bi2O3 sheets and Bi2S3 sheets can be also prepd. through simply modifying the synthetic recipe.  When employed as the sodium-ion battery anode material, the resultant BS-BO displays a reversible capacity of ∼630 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1.  In addn., the BS-BO demonstrates improved rate capability and enhanced cycle stability compared to its Bi2O3 sheets and Bi2S3 sheets counterparts.  The improved electrochem. performance can be ascribed to the built-in elec. field in the BS-BO heterostructure, which effectively facilitates the charge transport.  This work would shed light on the construction of novel heterostructures for high-performance sodium-ion batteries and other energy-related devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoCIEmoePEaYLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liaACf-Ml3rKA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXit1ymu74%253D&amp;md5=f781dd41028d13cc1f9c6d7d866947e8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref47"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref47'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">47</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit47" data-doi="10.1016/j.jallcom.2018.07.294"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, T.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sandwich-Like Graphene-Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> Hybrid Derived From (BiO)<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub>  Nanosheets as Advanced Anode Materials for Lithium/Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Bismuth sulfide (Bi2S3) has been considered a potential electrode material for Li storage due to its high theor. capacity and intriguing reaction mechanism.  In this work we have designed a Bi2S3@CNT nanocomposite as a sodium ion (Na-ion) battery anode material, and studied its electrochem. performance.  The layer structured Bi2S3 provides host sites for insertion of Na-ion and the carbon nanotube (CNT) in the Bi2S3@CNT nanocomposite serves as a highly conducting network to promote electron transport.                         cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchical CuBi2O4 microspheres as lithium-ion battery anodes with superior high-temperature electrochemical performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yin, Hong; Cao, Ming-Lei; Yu, Xiang-Xiang; Li, Chong; Shen, Yan; Zhu, Ming-Qiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">RSC Advances</span>
