        </div><div class="casAbstract">In the present report, hierarchical CuBi2O4 microspheres are prepd. through a hydrothermal route, and applied as anode materials for LIBs.  The hierarchical CuBi2O4 microspheres of diam. 2.0-4.0 μm are assembled by cryst. tetragonal nanoparticles with a size of 50-60 nm.  The electrochem. performance of the hierarchical CuBi2O4 microspheres shows strong temp.-dependence whereby higher temps. evidently enhance the electrochem. performance.  At an elevated temp. of 70 °C, a reversible capacity of 525.1 mA h g-1 has been achieved after 500 cycles at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1.  Even after being cycled at a high c.d. of 6.4 A g-1, the hierarchical CuBi2O4 microspheres are still able to deliver a capacity of 585 mA h g-1 when the c.d. is set back to 100 mA g-1.  The superior high-temp. electrochem. performance of the hierarchical CuBi2O4 microspheres is ascribed to their hierarchical structure and outstanding thermostability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr4nomVW8HcE7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liaACf-Ml3rKA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXjtl2gsLc%253D&amp;md5=477c4186c34d767ae259b071695a0d88</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref51'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit51" data-doi="10.1039/c7qm00128b"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, M.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, X.-X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, M.-Q.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Self-Standing Bi<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> Nanoparticles/Carbon Nanofiber Hybrid Films as a Binder-Free     Anode for Flexible Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Mater. Chem. Front.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>1</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1615</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1621</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/c7qm00128b</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D1%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D1615-1621%26journal%3DMater.%2BChem.%2BFront.%26author%3DH.%2BYin%26author%3DM.-L.%2BCao%26author%3DX.-X.%2BYu%26author%3DH.%2BZhao%26author%3DY.%2BShen%26author%3DC.%2BLi%26author%3DM.-Q.%2BZhu%26title%3DSelf-Standing%2BBi2O3%2BNanoparticles%252FCarbon%2BNanofiber%2BHybrid%2BFilms%2Bas%2Ba%2BBinder-Free%2B%2B%2B%2B%2BAnode%2Bfor%2BFlexible%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1039%252Fc7qm00128b&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c16316&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2Fc7qm00128b&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit51R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">51</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Self-standing Bi2O3 nanoparticles/carbon nanofiber hybrid films as a binder-free anode for flexible sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yin, Hong; Cao, Ming-Lei; Yu, Xiang-Xiang; Zhao, Han; Shen, Yan; Li, Chong; Zhu, Ming-Qiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Materials Chemistry Frontiers</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">1</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1615-1621</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">MCFAC5</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2052-1537</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A flexible binder-free film composed of bismuth oxide nanoparticles embedded in carbon nanofibers (Bi2O3/C) was prepd. by a feasible electrospinning method and directly used as a sodium ion battery (SIB) anode.  As a binder-free and flexible anode for SIBs, Bi2O3/C delivers a high reversible capacity of 430 mA h g-1 after 200 cycles at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1 and an exceptional rate capability of 230 mA h g-1 at 3200 mA g-1.  It has a stable capacity of 252 mA h g-1 after 50 cycles at 400 mA g-1 in a Na-ion full cell device.  The high capacity, good cyclability and rate capability are attributed to synergistic effects of the uniform distribution of ultra-small Bi2O3 nanoparticles (≈10 nm) in the carbon nanofibers and the conducting framework of 3-D interconnected carbon nanofibers, which can effectively alleviate the vol. expansion during sodiation/desodiation processes and maintain the high elec. cond. throughout the electrode.  This self-standing flexible Bi2O3/C nanocomposite electrode may hold great promise for high-performance SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoXBmh1KR9Jn7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgDtmT5Xa3vIg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhs1elsb7I&amp;md5=4f7c058dfc7ffa56d66fcac1dfe4eaab</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref52"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref52'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">52</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit52" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201100775"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Biswas, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, L.-D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kanatzidis, M. G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Tellurium-Free Thermoelectric: The Anisotropic N-Type Semiconductor Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub></span>. <i>Adv. Energy Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2012</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>2</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">634</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">638</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/aenm.201100775</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D2%26publication_year%3D2012%26pages%3D634-638%26journal%3DAdv.%2BEnergy%2BMater.%26author%3DK.%2BBiswas%26author%3DL.-D.%2BZhao%26author%3DM.%2BG.%2BKanatzidis%26title%3DTellurium-Free%2BThermoelectric%253A%2BThe%2BAnisotropic%2BN-Type%2BSemiconductor%2BBi2S3%26doi%3D10.1002%252Faenm.201100775&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c16316&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Faenm.201100775&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit52R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">52</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Tellurium-free thermoelectric: the anisotropic n-type semiconductor Bi2S3</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Biswas, Kanishka; Zhao, Li-Dong; Kanatzidis, Mercouri G.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">634-638</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADEMBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1614-6840</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">This paper reported the synthesis and promising thermoelec. (TE) properties of highly oriented bulk cryst. ingots of n-type bulk Bi2S3 doped with BiCl3.  Indeed, cryst. ingots of preferentially oriented Bi2S3 can be grown that allow optimization of the carrier concn. using BiCl3 as n-type dopant.  ZT values of up to ≈0.6 at 760 K can be achieved, which greatly exceed previously reported values of powder-processed Bi2S3 samples.  Electron mobilities as high as 640 cm2 V-1 s-1 were obsd. and doping Bi2S3 with BiCl3 leads to a significant increase in the elec. cond.  Further improvement of ZT values may be achieved by further suppression of the lattice thermal cond. by embedding second-phase endotaxial nanostructures in the Bi2S3 matrix as demonstrated recently in the case of PbS.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo-4hsp56PVXbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgDtmT5Xa3vIg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XptVOls74%253D&amp;md5=dd7d640555d1dd433267f6a9736aa3fa</span></div></div></div></div></li></ol></div><script type="text/javascript" nonce="90da8870ed46b325-SJC">window.refViewer={'ref1':['cit1'],'ref2':['cit2'],'ref3':['cit3'],'ref4':['cit4'],'ref5':['cit5'],'ref6':['cit6'],'ref7':['cit7'],'ref8':['cit8'],'ref9':['cit9'],'ref10':['cit10'],'ref11':['cit11'],'ref12':['cit12'],'ref13':['cit13'],'ref14':['cit14'],'ref15':['cit15'],'ref16':['cit16'],'ref17':['cit17'],'ref18':['cit18'],'ref19':['cit19'],'ref20':['cit20'],'ref21':['cit21'],'ref22':['cit22'],'ref23':['cit23'],'ref24':['cit24'],'ref25':['cit25'],'ref26':['cit26'],'ref27':['cit27'],'ref28':['cit28'],'ref29':['cit29'],'ref30':['cit30'],'ref31':['cit31'],'ref32':['cit32'],'ref33':['cit33'],'ref34':['cit34'],'ref35':['cit35'],'ref36':['cit36'],'ref37':['cit37'],'ref38':['cit38'],'ref39':['cit39'],'ref40':['cit40'],'ref41':['cit41'],'ref42':['cit42'],'ref43':['cit43'],'ref44':['cit44'],'ref45':['cit45'],'ref46':['cit46'],'ref47':['cit47'],'ref48':['cit48'],'ref49':['cit49'],'ref50':['cit50'],'ref51':['cit51'],'ref52':['cit52']}</script><div class="articleCitedByDropzone" data-pb-dropzone="articleCitedByDropzone"><div class="cited-by"><div class="article_content-header cited-content_header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div tabindex="0" class="article_content-title"><h2 id="citeThis">Cited By</h2><div class="article__copy"> <button class="article__copy__btn"><i aria-hidden="true" class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><div class="cited-by__content"><div class="sciteMetricsDropzone">

Mater. Interaces</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2012</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>4</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">3636</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">3642</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/am300722d</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Photocatalytic Synthesis of TiO2 and Reduced Graphene Oxide Nanocomposite for Lithium Ion Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Qiu, Jingxia; Zhang, Peng; Ling, Min; Li, Sheng; Liu, Porun; Zhao, Huijun; Zhang, Shanqing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3636-3642</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this work, we synthesized graphene oxide (GO) using the improved Hummers' oxidn. method.  TiO2 nanoparticles can be anchored on the GO sheets via the abundant oxygen-contg. functional groups such as epoxy, hydroxyl, carbonyl, and carboxyl groups on the GO sheets.  Using the TiO2 photocatalyst, the GO was photocatalytically reduced under UV illumination, leading to the prodn. of TiO2-reduced graphene oxide (TiO2-RGO) nanocomposite.  The as-prepd. TiO2, TiO2-GO, and TiO2-RGO nanocomposite were used to fabricate lithium-ion batteries as the active anode materials and their corresponding lithium ion insertion/extn. performance was evaluated.  The resultant lithium-ion batteries with the TiO2-RGO nanocomposite have more stable cyclic performance, larger reversible capacity, and better rate capability, compared with that of the pure TiO2 and TiO2-GO samples.  The electrochem. and materials characterization suggest that the graphene network provides efficient pathways for electron transfer, and the TiO2 nanoparticles prevent the restacking of the graphene nanosheets, resulting in the improvement in both elec. cond. and specific capacity, resp.  This work suggests that the TiO2-based photocatalytic method could be a simple, low-cost, and efficient approach for large-scale prodn. of anode materials for lithium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGriXTyK-a0pdbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljkh6JIM_pSBQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38Xpt1Churc%253D&amp;md5=ffdf7fa7fb3c5407cacc7276b01d0c02</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref3" class="rightTabRefNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit3" data-doi="10.1038/s41563-020-0729-1"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pawar, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ren, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Banerjee, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dufek, E.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have become increasingly important as next-generation energy storage systems for application in large-scale energy storage.  It is very crucial to develop an eco-friendly and green SIB technique with superior performance for sustainable future use.  Replacing the conventional inorg. electrode materials with green and safe org. electrodes will be a promising approach.  However, the poor electrochem. kinetics, unstable electrode-electrolyte interface, high soly. of the electrodes in the electrolyte, and large amt. of conductive carbon present great challenges for org. SIBs.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Here, we use a lithiophilic Bismuth graphite blend (Bi-Gr) substrate to replace lithiophobic Cu current collector to seed a uniform Li nucleation, and form a lithiophobic LiF-rich SEI rather than lithiophilic org.-rich SEI to suppress Li dendrite growth.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Topol. insulators have spurred worldwide interest, but their advantageous properties have scarcely been explored in terms of electrochem. energy storage, and their high-rate capability and long-term cycling stability still remain a significant challenge to harvest. p-Type topol. insulator SnSb2Te4 nanodots anchoring on few-layered graphene (SnSb2Te4/G) are synthesized as a stable anode for high-rate lithium-ion batteries and potassium-ion batteries through a ball-milling method.  These SnSb2Te4/G composite electrodes show ultralong cycle lifespan (478 mAh g-1 at 1 A g-1 after 1000 cycles) and excellent rate capability (remaining 373 mAh g-1 even at 10 A g-1) in Li-ion storage owing to the rapid ion transport accelerated by the PN heterojunction, virtual electron highways provided by the conductive topol. surface state, and extraordinary pseudocapacitive contribution, whose excellent phase reversibility is confirmed by synchrotron in situ X-ray powder diffraction.  Surprisingly, durable lifespan even at practical levels of mass loading (&gt;10 mg cm-2) for Li-ion storage and excellent K-ion storage performance are also obsd.         </div><div class="casAbstract">High-power Na-ion batteries capable of charging and discharging rapidly and durably are eagerly demanded to replace current Li-ion batteries.  However, poor activity and instable cycling of common Na anode materials represent a huge barrier for practical deployment.  A smart design of ordered nanotube arrays of Fe2O3 is presented as efficient Na anode, simply enabled by surface sulfurization.  The resulted heterostructure of oxide and sulfide spontaneously develops a built-in elec. field, which reduces the activation energy and accelerates charge transport significantly.  Benefiting from the synergy of ordered architecture and built-in elec. field, such arrays exhibit a large reversible capacity, a superior rate capability, and a high retention of 91% up to 200 cycles at a high rate of 5 A/g, outperforming most reported Fe oxide electrodes.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Ever-growing energy needs and depleting fossil-fuel resources demand the pursuit of sustainable energy alternatives, including both renewable energy sources and sustainable storage technologies.  It is therefore essential to incorporate material abundance, eco-efficient synthetic processes and life-cycle anal. into the design of new electrochem. storage systems.  At present, a few existing technologies address these issues, but in each case, fundamental and technol. hurdles remain to be overcome.  Here the authors provide an overview of the current state of energy storage from a sustainability perspective.  The authors introduce the notion of sustainability through discussion of the energy and environmental costs of state-of-the-art Li-ion batteries, considering elemental abundance, toxicity, synthetic methods and scalability.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A facile encapsulation of NiO nanoparticles in mesoporous carbon nanospheres (NiO/MCNs) is demonstrated.  Silicate-ion groups on nanosilica surface can react with Ni2+ ions to generate nickel silicate in situ around the SiO2 cores.  Such hybrids are introduced into polymer nanospheres prepd. by extended Stober strategy, followed by calcination and template removal to fabricate NiO/MCNs.  The typical NiO/MCNs have spherical morphol. (∼280 nm in diam.), uniform mesopores (5.9 nm), high sp. surface area (714 m2 g-1), and well-dispersed NiO nanoparticles (7.20 wt.%).  Package mesoporosity among the carbon spheres reduces ion diffusion distance, and the mesopores benefit fast ion transportation.  Besides, the introduction of NiO nanoparticles not only provides pseudocapacitance, but also increases the graphitization degree of the carbons and improves cryst. structure.  As a result, NiO/MCNs as supercapacitor electrodes show a high specific capacitance of 406 F g-1 at 1.0 A g-1 in 6 M KOH electrolyte, and it still maintains 315 F g-1 at a high loading c.d. of 20.0 A g-1.  Besides, NiO/MCN electrode retains ∼91.0% of the original capacity at 3.0 A g-1 after 10,000 cycles, exhibiting outstanding cycle stability.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Low energy d. is the key issue that needs to be addressed for sodium ion batteries.  Antimony sulfide (Sb2S3) with high theor. capacity is considered as an ideal anode, but it suffers from poor electrochem. activity and consequently, low energy d.  Simple hollow Sb2S3 structures with high electrochem. activity offer high gravimetric energy d., while large internal voids significantly decrease the volumetric energy d.  Here, multi-shell Sb2S3 was synthesized as an anode for sodium ion batteries, exhibiting much higher reversible capacity and gravimetric energy d. than the pristine Sb2S3. However, black phosphorus (bP), the 2D material with the largest anisotropy to date, is unstable as it degrades in air.  In this work we show that As2S3 is an interesting alternative, with a similar anisotropy to bP, while at the same time having a much higher chem. stability.  We probe the mech. and optical anisotropy in As2S3 by three distinct angular-resolved exptl. methods: Raman spectroscopy, at. force microscopy (AFM), and resonance frequency anal. However, capacity fading and cycling instability due to vol. variation during the lithiation/delithiation process still remain a great challenge.  Herein, we proposed a simple glucose assisted hydrothermal strategy and followed a post-treatment process to prep. hierarchical sulfur-doped carbon Bi2S3 (Bi2S3@SC) hollow nanotubes that self-assembled into sulfur-doped amorphous carbon coated Bi2S3 nanocrystals as building blocks.  Glucose plays a decisive role in the formation process of Bi2S3 nanocrystals and subsequent self-assembly, forming Bi2S3@SC hollow nanotubes.  The polysaccharide shell formed on the surface of Bi2S3 nanocrystals during the hydrothermal process was transformed into the sulfur-doped amorphous carbon layer after the post-treatment process.  Electrochem. tests reveal that the resulting composites exhibit excellent electrochem. performance with a highly reversible cycling capacity of ∼950 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1, as well as a good rate capability and significantly enhanced cycling stability derived from their unique structural features, thus demonstrating the potential of Bi2S3@SC hollow nanotubes as high performance anode materials for LIBs.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Regulating nanocrystal compn. with multiphase compds. is considered an efficient approach to enhance electrochem. performance and structure stability.  Nevertheless, the thorough understanding of significant reaction mechanisms and insight into the reason of enhanced performance is still urgent.  In this work, the bimetallic sulfide Bi2S3/MoS2 heterogeneous with abundant phase boundaries is successfully fabricated.  The in situ investigation of Na+-storage mechanism confirms that enormous phase boundaries are self-generated by compn. optimization and rational structural design.  More importantly, the full understanding of abundant phase boundaries on the enhanced electrochem. properties is explicitly unraveled by combining theor. anal. and exptl. results.  It confirms that the interior self-built-in elec.-field induced by phase boundaries can enhance the reaction kinetics and boost the charge transfer.  Besides, the Bi/Na2S interface is well-maintained by the homogeneously distributed phase boundaries, effectively improving the conversion/alloying reversibility and keeping integrity without agglomeration and pulverization.  As expected, the Bi2S3/MoS2 composite exhibits superior rate capability and long-cycling stability (323.4 mAh g-1 after long-term 1200 cycles at ultrahigh rate of 10 A g-1).         (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">19</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The sodium-ion capacitor (NIC) represents an important research approach to bridge the gap between batteries and capacitors, but is still limited by inferior energy behavior at high power, low volumetric performance, low electrode mass loading, and safety issues with conventional liq. electrolyte.  Herein, a high-performing, kinetically superior, and safer quasi-solid-state NIC utilizing the fast sodium storage in TiO2 and rapid ion adsorption on a biomass-derived porous carbon with a sodium-ion conducting P(VDF-HFP) gel polymer electrolyte is presented.  Owing to high mass loading, low graphene content in TiO2, and by overcoming the diffusion-limited sodium storage by surface limited storage enable the NIC to deliver an impressive volumetric energy of ≈89 Wh L-1 (94 Wh kg-1) based on total mass in both electrodes.  Also, a remarkable power of ≈9.4 kW L-1 (10 kW kg-1) while retaining an energy of ≈28.7 Wh L-1 (30.6 Wh kg-1) is attained.  Furthermore, the NIC shows a long-term stability both at room temp. and high temp. (50°C), outperforming conventional NICs.  This research opens new opportunities for applications of high-performing and safer NICs in next-generation storage devices requiring high energy at high power with high safety.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqRvYAITQ4IjbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljPs4pazzx2lQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhvVOiur%252FO&amp;md5=b56b5e2c6fa6c83b68e13d1d1aacd8cd</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref33" class="rightTabRefNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit33" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2016.08.115"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qiu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Effects of PPy, GO and PPy/GO Composites on The Negative Plate and on The High-Rate Partial-State-Of-Charge     Performance of Lead-Acid Batteries</span>. <i>Electrochim.         </div><div class="casAbstract">To improve the high-rate partial-state-of-charge (HRPSoC) performance of Pb-acid batteries for hybrid-elec. vehicles, graphene oxide (GO), polypyrrole (PPy) and three PPy/GO composites with different wt. ratio of pyrrole to GO (mpy/mGO) were selected as additives to form neg. plates and simulated test cells.  The effects of these additives on the electrochem. performance and the microstructure of the neg. plate and on the HRPSoC cycle performance of the simulated test cell were studied.  The microstructure of the neg. plate is changed with the addn. of different additives.  GO significantly increases the H (H2) evolution ability of the neg. plate, while PPy has the opposite effect.  The incorporation of the proper content of PPy with GO can effectively inhibit the H2 evolution of the neg. plate.  Also, adding different additives in the neg. plate also decreases its total impedance, accelerates the redox processes between Pb and PbSO4 on it and increases its specific capacitance.  GO and the PPy/GO composite with mpy/mGO = 1:1 (PG1) can significantly increase the HRPSoC cycle life of the simulated test cell.  Considering the H2 evolution performance and the HRPSoC cycle performance, the PPy/GO composites with a medium mpy/mGO ratio, such as PG1, may be the appropriate additives for the neg. plate of Pb-acid batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo8-jOSZFFETLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljPs4pazzx2lQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhsVegt7vO&amp;md5=ee576f2e9810ab1679d80239d2328dbc</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref34" class="rightTabRefNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit34" data-doi="10.1107/s0021889801002242"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Toby, B.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium ion batteries (SIBs) and lithium-sulfur (Li-S) batteries are considered as the most promising next-generation energy storage devices to displace the widely used lithium ion batteries due to their inherent advantages.  Here, polypyrrole-encapsulated amorphous Bi2S3 hollow spheres are prepd. by the sulfuration of Bi-glycol spheres with a polypyrrole (PPy) coating.  Benefiting from the unique hollow structure (Kirkendall effect) and the excellent cond. and flexibility of the PPy coating, this material can be applied in both SIBs and Li-S batteries.  For SIBs, the unconductive amorphous Bi2S3 is electrochem. reduced to conductive metallic Bi, leading to a Bi-PPy core-shell structure.  The resulting Bi acts as the main active material while the PPy coating accommodates the vol. variation of Bi during sodiation/desodiation.  For Li-S batteries, the outer double layer structure effectively prevents the dissoln. and "shuttle effect" of polysulfides by phys. contg. and chem. adsorbing polysulfides, and tolerates the vol. expansion of sulfur.  Meanwhile, the residual polyvinyl pyrrolidone in the prepn. process is chem. bonded with sulfur and exhibits the electrochem. properties, and results in addnl. discharging/charging capacity.  Thus, this multifunctional electrode shows excellent rate capability and cycling life in SIBs and Li-S batteries.                         rightTab-cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Bio-inspired engineering of Bi2S3-PPy yolk-shell composite for highly durable lithium and sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liang, Haichen; Ni, Jiangfeng; Li, Liang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Bismuth based compds. are uniquely interesting as anode materials in energy storage devices such as rechargeable batteries, owing to their large volumetric capacity and suitable operating potential higher than graphite.  How to achieve the high capacity durably and robustly remains an open challenge.  To address this issue, here we propose a bio-inspired material engineering of yolk-shell composite that consists of bismuth sulfide (Bi2S3) nanowire assembly intimately encapsulated in polypyrrole (PPy) shell.  The Bi2S3 yolk features a large void space and a short diffusion distance, while the PPy shell is highly conductive, flexible and resilient, allowing for the free vol. variation upon ion uptake and release.  When used as anode, the Bi2S3-PPy yolk-shell composite exhibits a superior Li storage cyclability (99% for 500 cycles) and a high rate capability (337 mAh g-1 at 10 C), outstripping any previous bismuth based materials.  This composite also affords a high reversible capacity of 591 mAh g-1 and a favorable durability for Na storage.  The discrepancy between Li and Na storage may correlate to the larger vol. change of Bi alloying with Na (∼250%) against with Li (∼110%).  This work offers a potential creative approach to engineering efficient electrodes for energy storage applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGovto5xM8CXa7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgOw8-Gjp6mCg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXit1Squ7Y%253D&amp;md5=949f4f32dff24a1486a9f12104b2d489</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref41" class="rightTabRefNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit41" data-doi="10.1039/c9nj04581c"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jin, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ju, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wen, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Q.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">MOF-Derived NiO-NiCo<sub>2</sub>O<sub>4</sub>@PPy Hollow     Polyhedron as a Sulfur Immobilizer for Lithium-Sulfur Batteries</span>. <i>New J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Bismuth sulfide (Bi2S3) is considered as an attractive anode material for sodium-ion battery (SIB) systems owing to its high theor. capacity (625 mAh g-1) and laminar structure for storing host ions.  However, capacity fading due to the large vol. change during long term cycling is a serious problem preventing the practical application of this material to SIBs.  Also, its elec. cond. is still unsatisfactory.  To solve those problems, the design of a Bi2S3/C composite with a yolk-shell type structure is proposed. Furthermore, the Bi2S3/C yolks-shell composite displays enhanced electrochem. performance as an SIB anode material and exhibits high stability during long-term cycling (282.4 mAh g-1 after 300 cycles at 0.2C) and improved rate capability (413.0 mAh g-1 at 10C). This work would shed light on the construction of novel heterostructures for high-performance sodium-ion batteries and other energy-related devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoCIEmoePEaYLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj0bsCq_Orfqg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXit1ymu74%253D&amp;md5=f781dd41028d13cc1f9c6d7d866947e8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref47"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref47" class="rightTabRefNumLink">47</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit47" data-doi="10.1016/j.jallcom.2018.07.294"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, T.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sandwich-Like Graphene-Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> Hybrid Derived From (BiO)<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub>  Nanosheets as Advanced Anode Materials for Lithium/Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.                 10.1016/j.matlet.2015.12.108</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A Bi2S3@CNT nanocomposite as anode material for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Wanli; Wang, Hao; Liu, Tingting; Gao, Lijun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Materials Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">167</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">102-105</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">MLETDJ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0167-577X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Bismuth sulfide (Bi2S3) has been considered a potential electrode material for Li storage due to its high theor. capacity and intriguing reaction mechanism.  In this work we have designed a Bi2S3@CNT nanocomposite as a sodium ion (Na-ion) battery anode material, and studied its electrochem. performance.  The layer structured Bi2S3 provides host sites for insertion of Na-ion and the carbon nanotube (CNT) in the Bi2S3@CNT nanocomposite serves as a highly conducting network to promote electron transport.  The results show that the Bi2S3@CNT nanocomposite exhibits a high and stable capacity in the 0.01-3 V (vs. Na/Na+) voltage region, notably outperforming the bare Bi2S3 material.  The Bi2S3@CNT nanocomposite as Na-ion anode material is able to discharge 84.4 mA h g-1 capacity at 60 mA g-1 over 60 full cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoWvw8d-zEHxrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj0bsCq_Orfqg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XksF2gtg%253D%253D&amp;md5=d5163e6c0a96f4baadaf14a7421a3c34</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref49" class="rightTabRefNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit49" data-doi="10.1039/c7nr06921a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Coupled Flower-Like Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> and Graphene Aerogels for Superior Sodium Storage Performance</span>. <i>Nanoscale</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>9</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">17694</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">17698</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/c7nr06921a</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Coupled flower-like Bi2S3 and graphene aerogels for superior sodium storage performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Yu; Fan, Lishuang; Wang, Pengxiang; Yin, Yanyou; Zhang, Xin Yu; Zhang, Naiqing; Sun, Kening</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">45</span>),

                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NANOHL</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2040-3372</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A hierarchically structured Bi2S3/graphene aerogel composite is constructed that shows excellent sodium storage properties.  Specifically, the composite delivers a stable reversible capacity of 397 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1 after 50 cycles and 348 mA h g-1 at 1 A g-1 after 120 cycles.  Furthermore, even at a high c.d. of 2 A g-1, a reversible capacity of 336 mA h g-1 is achieved.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqxEr6g60FaibVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj0bsCq_Orfqg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhslygu7%252FE&amp;md5=680dc0789c70ed20a8afed8540a3296b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref50"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref50" class="rightTabRefNumLink">50</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit50" data-doi="10.1039/c6ra27216a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, M.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, X.-X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, M.-Q.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hierarchical CuBi<sub>2</sub>O<sub>4</sub> Microspheres as Lithium-Ion Battery Anodes with Superior High-Temperature Electrochemical  Performance</span>. <i>RSC Adv.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>7</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">13250</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">13256</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/c6ra27216a</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchical CuBi2O4 microspheres as lithium-ion battery anodes with superior high-temperature electrochemical performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yin, Hong; Cao, Ming-Lei; Yu, Xiang-Xiang; Li, Chong; Shen, Yan; Zhu, Ming-Qiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">RSC Advances</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">22</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In the present report, hierarchical CuBi2O4 microspheres are prepd. through a hydrothermal route, and applied as anode materials for LIBs.  The hierarchical CuBi2O4 microspheres of diam. 2.0-4.0 μm are assembled by cryst. tetragonal nanoparticles with a size of 50-60 nm.  The electrochem. performance of the hierarchical CuBi2O4 microspheres shows strong temp.-dependence whereby higher temps. evidently enhance the electrochem. performance.  At an elevated temp. of 70 °C, a reversible capacity of 525.1 mA h g-1 has been achieved after 500 cycles at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1.  Even after being cycled at a high c.d. of 6.4 A g-1, the hierarchical CuBi2O4 microspheres are still able to deliver a capacity of 585 mA h g-1 when the c.d. is set back to 100 mA g-1.  The superior high-temp. electrochem. performance of the hierarchical CuBi2O4 microspheres is ascribed to their hierarchical structure and outstanding thermostability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr4nomVW8HcE7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj0bsCq_Orfqg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXjtl2gsLc%253D&amp;md5=477c4186c34d767ae259b071695a0d88</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref51" class="rightTabRefNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit51" data-doi="10.1039/c7qm00128b"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, M.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, X.-X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, M.-Q.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Self-Standing Bi<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> Nanoparticles/Carbon Nanofiber Hybrid Films as a Binder-Free     Anode for Flexible Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Mater. Chem. Front.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>1</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1615</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1621</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/c7qm00128b</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit51R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">51</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Self-standing Bi2O3 nanoparticles/carbon nanofiber hybrid films as a binder-free anode for flexible sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yin, Hong; Cao, Ming-Lei; Yu, Xiang-Xiang; Zhao, Han; Shen, Yan; Li, Chong; Zhu, Ming-Qiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Materials Chemistry Frontiers</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">1</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1615-1621</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">MCFAC5</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2052-1537</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A flexible binder-free film composed of bismuth oxide nanoparticles embedded in carbon nanofibers (Bi2O3/C) was prepd. by a feasible electrospinning method and directly used as a sodium ion battery (SIB) anode.  As a binder-free and flexible anode for SIBs, Bi2O3/C delivers a high reversible capacity of 430 mA h g-1 after 200 cycles at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1 and an exceptional rate capability of 230 mA h g-1 at 3200 mA g-1.  It has a stable capacity of 252 mA h g-1 after 50 cycles at 400 mA g-1 in a Na-ion full cell device.  The high capacity, good cyclability and rate capability are attributed to synergistic effects of the uniform distribution of ultra-small Bi2O3 nanoparticles (≈10 nm) in the carbon nanofibers and the conducting framework of 3-D interconnected carbon nanofibers, which can effectively alleviate the vol. expansion during sodiation/desodiation processes and maintain the high elec. cond. throughout the electrode.  This self-standing flexible Bi2O3/C nanocomposite electrode may hold great promise for high-performance SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoXBmh1KR9Jn7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj0bsCq_Orfqg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhs1elsb7I&amp;md5=4f7c058dfc7ffa56d66fcac1dfe4eaab</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref52"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref52" class="rightTabRefNumLink">52</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit52" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201100775"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Biswas, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, L.-D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kanatzidis, M. G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Tellurium-Free Thermoelectric: The Anisotropic N-Type Semiconductor Bi<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub></span>. <i>Adv. Energy Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2012</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>2</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">634</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">638</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/aenm.201100775</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit52R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">52</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Tellurium-free thermoelectric: the anisotropic n-type semiconductor Bi2S3</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Biswas, Kanishka; Zhao, Li-Dong; Kanatzidis, Mercouri G.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">634-638</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADEMBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1614-6840</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">This paper reported the synthesis and promising thermoelec. (TE) properties of highly oriented bulk cryst. ingots of n-type bulk Bi2S3 doped with BiCl3.  Indeed, cryst. ingots of preferentially oriented Bi2S3 can be grown that allow optimization of the carrier concn. using BiCl3 as n-type dopant.  ZT values of up to ≈0.6 at 760 K can be achieved, which greatly exceed previously reported values of powder-processed Bi2S3 samples.  Electron mobilities as high as 640 cm2 V-1 s-1 were obsd. and doping Bi2S3 with BiCl3 leads to a significant increase in the elec. cond.  Further improvement of ZT values may be achieved by further suppression of the lattice thermal cond. by embedding second-phase endotaxial nanostructures in the Bi2S3 matrix as demonstrated recently in the case of PbS.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®"         <script nonce="90da8870ed46b325-SJC">
(function(){
	
	/*Event Tracking for RIS menu dropdown - Article pages*/

	$('.cit-download-dropdown_button').on('click',function(e)
	{	
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':'Main'});

	});


	$('.cit-download-dropdown_content ul li').on('click',function(e)
	{	
	//	e.preventDefault();
	    var idx = $(this).index();
	    
	    var label = '';
	    if (idx === 0 ) {
	    	label = 'Citation';
	    } else if (idx === 1 ) {
	    	label = 'Abstract';
	    } else if (idx === 2 ) {
	    	label = 'Reference';
	    } else if (idx === 3 ) {
	    	label = 'More Options';
	    }
	   
	   gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':label});
	});

	$('.header_contnav-next a').on('click', function(e){
        e.preventDefault();
        gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Right Arrow'});
	}); 

 	$('.header_contnav-pre a').on('click', function(e){
	    e.preventDefault();
	     gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Left Arrow'});
	}); 

	$('.share_button').on('click', function(e){
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Share'});
	});

	$("#pane-m1con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Figures'});
	});

	$("#pane-m2con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'References'});
	});

	$("#pane-m3con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Supporting Info'});
	});

	$('.tab__close').on('click', function(){
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Close'});
	}); 



})();

</script>

        <span class="system-message-date">Thursday, February 06, 2025</span>
        <p>Please be aware that pubs.acs.org is undergoing maintenance from Saturday February 1 to Monday Febraury 3, that may have an impact on your experience. During this time, you may not be able to access certain features like login, purchasing single articles, saving searches or running existing saved searches, modifying your e-Alert preferences, or accessing Librarian administrative functions. <script nonce="90da8870ed46b325-SJC">
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function(){
    // Function to get a Human readable formatted date
    function getFormattedDateForMaintenance() {
        let today = new Date();
        let dd = String(today.getDate()).padStart(2, '0');
        //January is 0
        let mm = String(today.getMonth() + 1).padStart(2, '0'); 
        let yyyy = today.getFullYear();
        
        let daysOfWeek = ['Sunday', 'Monday', 'Tuesday', 'Wednesday', 'Thursday', 'Friday', 'Saturday'];
        let monthsOfYear = ['January', 'February', 'March', 'April', 'May', 'June', 'July', 'August', 'September', 'October', 'November', 'December'];

        let dayOfWeek = daysOfWeek[today.getDay()];
        let monthOfYear = monthsOfYear[today.getMonth()];

        return dayOfWeek + ', ' + monthOfYear + ' ' + dd + ', ' + yyyy;
    }
    
    // Insert the date into the .system-message-date element
    document.querySelector('.system-message-date').innerText = getFormattedDateForMaintenance();
});
</script>

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="90da8870ed46b325-SJC">
"use strict"
//Script checks gdpr cookie and submits form
	/* 
	Create an in-page pop-up message, only for the InfoCentral homepage, that will gather email registrants for the library marketing list.
	 
	Needs the end point
	*/

var infoCentralCapture = (function() {

    //Detect mobile device
    window.mobilecheck = function() {
        var check = false;
        (function(a){if(/(android|bb\d+|meego).+mobile|avantgo|bada\/|blackberry|blazer|compal|elaine|fennec|hiptop|iemobile|ip(hone|od)|iris|kindle|lge |maemo|midp|mmp|mobile.+firefox|netfront|opera wa|abac|ac(er|oo|s\-)|ai(ko|rn)|al(av|ca|co)|amoi|an(ex|ny|yw)|aptu|ar(ch|go)|as(te|us)|attw|au(di|\-m|r |s )|avan|be(ck|ll|nq)|bi(lb|rd)|bl(ac|az)|br(e|v)w|bumb|bw\-(n|u)|c55\/|capi|ccwa|cdm\-|cell|chtm|cldc|cmd\-|co(mp|nd)|craw|da(it|ll|ng)|dbte|dc\-s|devi|dica|dmob|do(c|p)o|ds(12|\-d)|el(49|ai)|em(l2|ul)|er(ic|k0)|esl8|ez([4-7]0|os|wa|ze)|fetc|fly(\-|_)|g1 u|g560|gene|gf\-5|g\-mo|go(\.w|od)|gr(ad|un)|haie|hcit|hd\-(m|p|t)|hei\-|hi(pt|ta)|hp( i|ip)|hs\-c|ht(c(\-| |_|a|g|p|s|t)|tp)|hu(aw|tc)|i\-(20|go|ma)|i230|iac( |\-|\/)|ibro|idea|ig01|ikom|im1k|inno|ipaq|iris|ja(t|v)a|jbro|jemu|jigs|kddi|keji|kgt( |\/)|klon|kpt |kwc\-|kyo(c|k)|le(no|xi)|lg( g|\/(k|l|u)|50|54|\-[a-w])|libw|lynx|m1\-w|m3ga|m50\/|ma(te|ui|xo)|mc(01|21|ca)|m\-cr|me(rc|ri)|mi(o8|oa|ts)|mmef|mo(01|02|bi|de|do|t(\-| |o|v)|zz)|mt(50|p1|v )|mwbp|mywa|n10[0-2]|n20[2-3]|n30(0|2)|n50(0|2|5)|n7(0(0|1)|10)|ne((c|m)\-|on|tf|wf|wg|wt)|nok(6|i)|nzph|o2im|op(ti|wv)|oran|owg1|p800|pan(a|d|t)|pdxg|pg(13|\-([1-8]|c))|phil|pire|pl(ay|uc)|pn\-2|po(ck|rt|se)|prox|psio|pt\-g|qa\-a|qc(07|12|21|32|60|\-[2-7]|i\-)|qtek|r380|r600|raks|rim9|ro(ve|zo)|s55\/|sa(ge|ma|mm|ms|ny|va)|sc(01|h\-|oo|p\-)|sdk\/|se(c(\-|0|1)|47|mc|nd|ri)|sgh\-|shar|sie(\-|m)|sk\-0|sl(45|id)|sm(al|ar|b3|it|t5)|so(ft|ny)|sp(01|h\-|v\-|v )|sy(01|mb)|t2(18|50)|t6(00|10|18)|ta(gt|lk)|tcl\-|tdg\-|tel(i|m)|tim\-|t\-mo|to(pl|sh)|ts(70|m\-|m3|m5)|tx\-9|up(\.b|g1|si)|utst|v400|v750|veri|vi(rg|te)|vk(40|5[0-3]|\-v)|vm40|voda|vulc|vx(52|53|60|61|70|80|81|83|85|98)|w3c(\-| )|webc|whit|wi(g |nc|nw)|wmlb|wonu|x700|yas\-|your|zeto|zte\-/i.test(a.substr(0,4))) check = true;})(navigator.userAgent||navigator.vendor||window.opera);
              return check;
        };

    var _isMobile = window.mobilecheck();
    if (_isMobile) {
        $('#gdpr-message-modal').addClass('mobile');
    }

    var emailValid = "",
        time = 3000,
        btnStatus = true,
        errorStatus = false,
        errormessage = "<p class='gdpr_err'><b>Please Enter a valid email address<b><p>";

    function init() {
        setTimeout(function() {
            var cookieExist = getCookie("gdpr");
            if (cookieExist) {
                //console.log("gdpr cookie exist");
                return false;
            } else {
                //console.log("gdpr cookie does not exist")
                gdprMessage();
            }
            //Events
            $('#closebtn').on("click", hideForm);

            //Handle submit
            $('#gdpr-message-btn').on("click", function(event) {
                handleClick();
            });

            // //Hide if clicked outside div - TO DO stop handling click after submit
            // $(document).click(function(event) {
            // 	event.stopPropagation();
            //   console.log(event.target);
            //   if (!$(event.target).closest("#gdpr-message-content").length) {
            //     $("body").find("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
            //     $(this).off();
            //   }
            // });
            $('#gdpr-con-btn').click(function() {
                setCookie("gdpr", "true");
                hideForm();
            });
        }, time);
    }

    //Show the message
    function gdprMessage() {
        //console.log("Show GDPR Message");
        var tMessage, emailInput, messageButton, ewrap;

        $('#gdpr-message-modal').show();
    }

    function handleClick() {
        //console.log($("#gdpr-input").val());
        emailValid = validateEmail($("#gdpr-input").val());
        if (emailValid) {
            //Submit the form
            //Hide form
            if ($('.gdpr_err')) {
                $('.gdpr_err').hide();
            }

            $("#gdpr-message-content")
                //If successful then...
            setCookie("gdpr", "true");
            //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid + " submiting form");
        } else {
            //Show error message
            gdprErrorMessage();
            //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid);
        }
    }

    function gdprErrorMessage() {
        if (errorStatus) {
            return false;
        } else {
            errorStatus = true;
            $("#gdpr-message-content").append(errormessage);
        }
    }

    function validateEmail(email) {
        var re = /^(([^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+(\.[^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+)*)|(".+"))@((\[[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\])|(([a-zA-Z\-0-9]+\.)+[a-zA-Z]{2,}))$/;
        return re.test(String(email).toLowerCase());
    }

    function setCookie(name, value) {
        var expires = "";
        expires = "; expires=Fri, 31 Dec 9999 23:59:59 GMT";
        document.cookie = name + "=" + (value || "") + expires + "; path=/";
    }

    function getCookie(name) {
        var match = document.cookie.match(new RegExp(name + '=([^;]+)'));
        if (match) return match[1];
    }

    function hideForm() { //And set cookie
        $('#gdpr-message-modal').hide();
        setCookie("gdpr", "false");
        gtag('event', 'GDPR Modal', { 'event_category': 'Pubs GDPR', 'event_label':'GDPR Dismissal'});
    }

    return {
        init: init
    }
})();

$(document).ready(infoCentralCapture.init);
</script>


                    
                        



        
        <script nonce="90da8870ed46b325-SJC">
var currentJournal = "ACS Applied Materials &amp;amp; Interfaces";
$(".citationLinks > a").click(function(e){
    if($(this).text() === "ACS Full Text ") {
        gtag('event', 'ACS Full Text', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Crossref") {
        gtag('event', 'Crossref', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "CAS") {
        gtag('event', 'CAS', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "PubMed") {
        gtag('event', 'PubMed', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Google Scholar") {
        gtag('event', 'Google Scholar', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).hasClass("issue-item_open-url") === true) {
        gtag('event', 'OpenURL', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
});
</script>

                    
                        



        
        <script nonce="90da8870ed46b325-SJC">
$(document).ready(function(){
    var cookie = "";
    var uri = "/doi/full/10.1021/html_original_uri?id=123";
    console.log("ACSPubs2 start");
    $.getJSON('https://extreme-ip-lookup.com/json/', function(data, status) {
            if ( status == 'success' ) {
                $.each(data, function(i, field){
                    cookie=cookie.concat(i+' = '+field+" - ");
                });
                
            } else {
                    cookie=status;
            }

            cookie1 = cookie;
            cookie = cookie1 + "; path=/; domain=.acs.org";
            //document.cookie = "ACSPubs2= "+ btoa(cookie) ;
            $.cookie("ACSPubs2", btoa(cookie), {path: '/'}); // Session cookie valid across the entire site.
            //TODO send cookie val to the controller for logging
            console.log("ACSPubs2 success");
    })
    .fail(function(xx, status, err){
        cookie="error: 127.0.0.1";
        //document.cookie = "ACSPubs2= "+ btoa(cookie) ;
        $.cookie("ACSPubs2", btoa(cookie), {path: '/'}); // Session cookie valid across the entire site.
        console.log("ACSPubs2 failed");
        //TODO send cookie val to the controller for logging
    });
});    
</script>
